Fixed: now reports `changed` (full entry text differs) alongside added/removed; the sync runner exits 1 in `--check` mode and writes in normal mode if any of the three is non-empty. **When the fixed sync ran against the existing registry, it surfaced 10 silently-misclassified tools** whose `.braid` files declared `@policy(WRITE_OPERATIONS)` but were stored as `READ_ONLY`: `process_inbound_communication` (communications.braid), `analyze_document` (documents.braid), `send_document_for_signing` (docuseal.braid), `draft_email` (email-drafting.braid), `full_lifecycle_advance` (lifecycle.braid), `clear_report_cache` (reports.braid), `initiate_call` and `call_contact` (telephony.braid), `invite_user` (users.braid), `instantiate_workflow_template` (workflows.braid). **This is a real security finding** ŌĆö these tools were running under `READ_ONLY` policy at runtime, potentially bypassing the write-operation capability gate. The `.braid` authors had it right; the generator was silently downgrading them. **Tests** (`braid-llm-kit/tools/__tests__/registry-policy-inference.test.js`, 13 passing): @policy annotation precedence over heuristic, heuristic fallback for legacy files, expanded write verbs, DELETE_OPERATIONS coercion, unknown policy rejection, edge cases (null entries, empty args, non-array args). All 148 production braid integration tests still pass ŌĆö including the four-test gauntlet on the new `docuseal.braid` file (parses, has @policy, effectful functions have tenant param, passes type checking). `npm run braid:sync` regenerated `backend/lib/braid/registry.js` (126 ŌåÆ 129 functions; 23 ŌåÆ 24 files). **Closes 4VD-10.**

### Changed

- **DocuSeal webhook tenant resolution: platform-secret path with legacy fallback (4VD-32 Phase B) (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook-platform-secret.test.js`)**: 4VD-15 moved DocuSeal API access to a single platform-level key + `external_id`-stamped tenant isolation, but the webhook signature path was still iterating `tenant_integrations[type=docuseal, is_active=true]` rows trying each tenant's `webhook_secret` in turn. That model assumes per-tenant DocuSeal user accounts (each with their own webhook_secret entered into DocuSeal admin) ŌĆö which is incompatible with a single shared DocuSeal install where there's only ONE webhook URL configured upstream. **Added** `resolveTenantViaPlatformSecret(supabase, rawBody, signatureHeader, parsedPayload?)`: when `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` is set, the function verifies the signature against that single secret (supports both static-secret mode and `sha256=<hex>` HMAC mode via the existing `verifyDocusealSignature`), then resolves the tenant by parsing the payload's `data.submission_id` (or `data.id` as fallback) and looking up `docuseal_submissions.tenant_id` for that submission. Returns `{ tenant_id, via: 'platform_secret' }` on success, `null` otherwise. **Handler integration**: the `router.post('/docuseal', ...)` entry point now calls `resolveTenantViaPlatformSecret` first; if it returns null, falls through to the legacy `resolveTenantFromSignature` (which iterates `tenant_integrations` rows). Both paths annotate their result with `via:` so log analysis can distinguish migration-window deliveries from steady-state. **Migration safety** ŌĆö both paths run simultaneously: existing tenant_integrations rows keep verifying inbound webhooks until the operator (a) generates and sets `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` in Doppler dev/staging/prod and (b) pastes the same value into DocuSeal admin ŌåÆ Settings ŌåÆ Webhooks. The DELETE migration on the legacy rows + UI write-path teardown lands in 4VD-32 Phase C, blocked on (a)+(b). **Tests** (`docuseal-webhook-platform-secret.test.js`, 13 passing): env-gating (returns null when `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_WEBHOOK_SECRET` unset, no Supabase query fired); env-gating without signature header (no Supabase query); static-secret mismatch (no DB query); static-secret match ŌåÆ tenant resolved from `docuseal_submissions` row; HMAC `sha256=` match ŌåÆ tenant resolved; HMAC computed with wrong secret rejected; payload missing submission id ŌåÆ null; payload `data.id` fallback when `data.submission_id` absent; unknown submission id ŌåÆ null (lookup happened but no row matched); supabase error during lookup ŌåÆ null (graceful degrade); string `rawBody` accepted alongside Buffer; malformed JSON ŌåÆ null without throw; `parsedPayload` argument bypasses re-parse. Full DocuSeal backend suite still green ŌĆö 86/86 across `docuseal-webhook.test.js`, `docuseal-events.test.js`, `docuseal-webhook-collapse.test.js`, `docuseal-external-id.test.js`, `docuseal-webhook-platform-secret.test.js`. **In progress towards 4VD-32**.

- **DocuSeal activity timeline collapses 4 events into 1 status-tracking row + adds "Follow up by" due date + populates `related_name` so timeline hyperlink shows the actual entity name (4VD-33 + 4VD-39) (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/lib/docusealActivityDueAt.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/docusealActivityDueAt.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook-collapse.test.js`, `src/components/docuseal/SendDocumentDialog.jsx`)**: Each DocuSeal lifecycle event used to insert a separate `activities` row (sent / viewed / signed / completed ŌåÆ up to 4 rows for one document). Now ONE row per submission, status flows through it. **Send route** (`docuseal.js:351`) inserts the row with `status='pending'`, `due_at=<computed>`, and pre-creates metadata slots (`sent_at`, `viewed_at`, `signed_at`, `completed_at`, `declined_at`) so the webhook can populate them in place. **Webhook** (`docuseal-webhook.js:157` `createActivity`) refactored to UPDATE-OR-INSERT: looks up the row by `tenant_id` + `metadata->>docuseal_submission_id`, updates type/subject/body/status and merges the lifecycle timestamp into metadata. Status state machine: `pending` (sent) ŌåÆ `pending` (viewed) ŌåÆ `completed` (signed/completed) OR `cancelled` (declined/expired/failed). The 1-hour viewed dedupe is gone ŌĆö there's only one row per submission now, multiple `viewed` events simply re-stamp `metadata.viewed_at` (last view wins, which is the more useful semantic anyway). Fallback INSERT path kept for resilience: if no row exists when a webhook arrives (race with the send-side INSERT, or its INSERT failed), webhook handler inserts so the lifecycle event isn't lost. **Due date default**: new `backend/lib/docusealActivityDueAt.js` exports `computeDocumentDueFields(supabase, tenantId)` which loads `tenants.timezone` (gracefully degrades to `UTC` if column missing) and returns `{ due_date, due_time }` (wall-clock strings: `YYYY-MM-DD` + `17:00:00`) in the tenant's timezone. Pure stdlib (`Intl.DateTimeFormat`) ŌĆö handles DST transitions correctly. **Schema fit**: the activities table stores `due_date date` + `due_time time` (matching the convention used by `calcom-webhook.js:259`), so this PR uses those existing columns rather than adding a new `due_at timestamptz`. Verified prod + staging schemas: both have `due_date` (date) + `due_time` (time), no `due_at`. Frontend `SendDocumentDialog` has a "Follow up by" `datetime-local` input defaulting to next-day 5pm in the user's browser timezone; the value is split on `T` into `due_date` + `due_time` (no timezone math because `datetime-local` is wall-clock by definition) and sent as separate fields. Backend uses the override if both fields are valid, falls back to the tenant-tz default. **Tests**: 16 new in `docusealActivityDueAt.test.js` (UTC + EDT/EST DST + JST + month/year boundaries + invalid TZ fallback + tenants.timezone column-missing degrade); 17 new in `docuseal-webhook-collapse.test.js` (status mapping for each event, metadata-timestamp slot mapping, lifecycle progression). All 149 docuseal tests pass (was 75 before this PR landed; +74 from the new + adjusted suites). **Backfill of existing multi-row submissions**: deferred (issue says optional; staging history is destructible per project preference). **Activity-timeline UI sub-status pills** (separate acceptance criterion): not in this PR ŌĆö the row's metadata now carries `viewed_at` / `signed_at` / `completed_at`, so the timeline component can render pills as a follow-up without further backend changes. **4VD-39 fold-in**: new `backend/lib/resolveRelatedEntityFields.js` helper consolidates the entity ŌåÆ display-name lookup pattern that was previously inline in `calcom-webhook.js`, `activities.v2.js`, and `workflowExecutionService.js`. Both the send route and the webhook (UPDATE + fallback-INSERT paths) now call it to populate `related_name` and `related_email` on the activity row. Activities timeline reads `activity.related_name` and falls back to `View {entity}` when null ŌĆö so before this change every DocuSeal activity rendered as "View Lead" / "View Contact". Now it shows the actual lead/contact/account name as the hyperlink. Helper degrades gracefully (returns null) on any lookup failure so the activity insert/update still proceeds. The webhook UPDATE path also opportunistically backfills `related_name`/`related_email` on rows that pre-date the fix (only when the row currently has them blank, to avoid clobbering operator edits). 14 new tests in `backend/__tests__/lib/resolveRelatedEntityFields.test.js`: lead/contact/account/opportunity/bizdev_source name composition, partial-name handling, all-null degrade, supabase error/throw degrade, tenant-id filter on the lookup query (defense against cross-tenant id leaks). **Closes 4VD-33 and 4VD-39.**

### Fixed

- **DocuSeal activity timeline shows the actual template name instead of "unnamed template" (4VD-34) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-resolve-template-name.test.js`)**: Activity rows for sent documents read `Document sent ŌĆö unnamed template` because DocuSeal Community's `POST /api/submissions` response does NOT include the template name (only `submission_id`, `slug`, `embed_src`, `email`). Verified live: the response shape returns the submitters array but no `template.name` or `template_name` field ŌĆö so the optimistic read at `docuseal.js:235` always fell through to `null`, got persisted to `docuseal_submissions.template_name`, and the activity-subject builder at `docuseal-webhook.js:174` rendered the "unnamed template" fallback. **Fix (Option C from the spec)**: new `resolveTemplateNameForTenant()` helper that uses the existing per-tenant `templatesCache` (60s TTL, populated by `GET /api/docuseal/templates` when the user opens the dropdown) as the primary source. Hot path is O(1) cache lookup with zero extra HTTP ŌĆö the user just selected from the dropdown, so the cache is almost always warm at the moment they click Send. Cold-cache or cache-miss-for-id paths fall through to one upstream `GET /api/templates?external_id=<tenantId>&limit=200` call, populate the same cache, then resolve. Send route at line 235 keeps an optimistic read of any `template.name` / `template_name` DocuSeal might add in future versions, then falls through to the resolver. **Tenant isolation defense**: `fetchDocusealTemplates` always passes `externalId: tenantId`, so a `template_id` from another tenant simply won't appear in the result and the resolver returns `null` ŌĆö Option C surfaces cross-tenant template_id leaks naturally as a defense-in-depth layer beyond the upstream-side `external_id` filter from 4VD-15. **Graceful degrade**: upstream errors (5xx, 401, network throw) are caught and return `null` so the submission still completes ŌĆö same behaviour as before, just with better hot-path semantics. **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-resolve-template-name.test.js`, 11 passing): warm cache returns name without firing any fetch (the assertion uses a fetch double that throws if invoked); cache hit but unknown template_id falls through to fresh fetch; cold cache fires fetch with `external_id=tenantId`; numeric vs string template_id both resolve; cross-tenant template_id resolves to null; per-tenant cache keyed correctly (Tenant B fetch doesn't see Tenant A entries); upstream 5xx/401/network-throw all return null gracefully. Existing 43 docuseal tests continue to pass ŌĆö no regression. **Backfill of historic rows** (4VD-34 acceptance criterion): not done in this commit. Staging history is destructible per project preference; the fix takes effect on next send. If a backfill becomes useful later, the same `resolveTemplateNameForTenant` helper can be called from a one-off script over `WHERE template_name IS NULL`. **Closes 4VD-34.**

- **VPS-1 staging outage 2026-05-07 ŌĆö root cause identified as Coolify v4.3.5 auto-upgrade flipping `is_auto_deploy_enabled=true` on staging apps + drift guard installed (4VD-37) (`scripts/install-coolify-drift-guard.ps1`, `scripts/probe-coolify-{drift-cause,upgrade-evidence,code-paths,final-forensic}.ps1`, `scripts/fix-auto-deploy-setting.ps1`, `backend/__tests__/ops/coolify-drift-guard.test.js`)**: 4VD-24's defense-in-depth set `is_auto_deploy_enabled=false` on application_settings rows for staging apps 12 (staging-backend-heavy), 13 (staging-app-fast), 15 (staging-braid), 19 (staging-litellm) so Coolify wouldn't double-fire deploys (its own git-push listener AND the CI workflow `deploy-staging.yml` from 4VD-30 firing on the same push would queue two builds, busting Zap's 5.5-core hypervisor cap on VPS-1). On 2026-05-07 16:49 UTC, deploys 198 (`is_webhook=t, force_rebuild=f`) + 199 (`is_webhook=f, force_rebuild=t`) at the same SHA `7ce897c1` confirmed the double-fire pattern was back; staging-app + all 4 Coolify apps showed `exited:unhealthy`, Cloudflare returned 530. **Forensics** (probe scripts above + Coolify v4.3.5 source paths inside `coolify` container at `/var/www/html/app/Models/ApplicationSetting.php`, `/var/www/html/app/Models/Application.php` line 339-342, `/var/www/html/app/Livewire/Project/Application/Advanced.php`, `/var/www/html/app/Http/Controllers/Api/ApplicationsController.php`, `/var/www/html/database/migrations/2023_03_27_081717_create_application_settings_table.php`): the `coolify` container restarted at 2026-05-06 03:15:45 UTC with image `e466c5d5d831` (`ghcr.io/coollabsio/coolify:latest`, `org.opencontainers.image.version=v4.3.5-2471289315`); `/data/coolify/source/.env` was rewritten at 03:14 UTC. The DDL default for `is_auto_deploy_enabled` is `true` (set in the 2023 create-table migration), and `Application::create`'s `static::created` event hook calls `ApplicationSetting::create(['application_id' => ...])` with no explicit value ŌĆö picking up the DDL default. No 2026-month migration on application_settings was run. The `activity_log` table (spatie/activitylog) showed 8 rows during the 03:14-03:15 boot window but they were all SSL cert installs and docker network cleanup tasks ŌĆö none were ApplicationSetting writes. No code path in `app/Console`, `app/Jobs`, `app/Providers`, no model observer, no seeder writes `is_auto_deploy_enabled` to existing rows ŌĆö only `Application::create`'s `static::created` hook (line 339-342) and the UI/API write paths. The exact mechanism by which Coolify reset existing rows on upgrade is not visible in the in-container code (likely a hidden settings refresh during the autoupdate process, a Redis cache rebuild that propagated stale defaults, or a UI-state reset). **Fix applied**: (1) `scripts/fix-auto-deploy-setting.ps1` immediately restored `is_auto_deploy_enabled=false` on apps 12, 13, 15, 19 via `UPDATE application_settings ... RETURNING application_id, is_auto_deploy_enabled` (confirmed 2026-05-07 18:40:18 UTC); deploy 200 fired single-row, finished in 8m25s; new bundle `entry-kJDbeObd.js` live; all 4 staging apps `running:healthy`. (2) **`scripts/install-coolify-drift-guard.ps1`** deploys `/usr/local/bin/coolify-auto-deploy-drift-guard.sh` to VPS-2 ŌĆö runs every 5 minutes via `coolify-drift-guard.timer` (also 1 min after boot, `Persistent=true` so missed runs after a VPS-2 reboot get caught up), exits 0 silently when state is healthy (zero log noise on the 99.9% healthy path), and on drift detection logs to BOTH `/var/log/coolify-drift-guard.log` AND journalctl with `logger -t coolify-drift-guard -p user.warning` for the detection event and `user.notice` for the correction confirmation, then runs the same idempotent UPDATE filter (`WHERE application_id IN (...) AND is_auto_deploy_enabled = true RETURNING application_id`). Installer self-tests end-to-end before declaring success: induces drift on app 13, runs guard manually, asserts final state has all 4 apps at `is_auto_deploy_enabled=false`. Self-test passed 2026-05-07 20:14:19 UTC. (3) **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/ops/coolify-drift-guard.test.js`, 9 passing): contract pin on the installer's heredoc ŌĆö staging app IDs match (12,13,15,19); detection SQL filters by both `application_id IN (...)` and `is_auto_deploy_enabled = true`; correction UPDATE is idempotent (only flips drifted rows, not all rows); healthy-path early-exit comes BEFORE any tee/logger call (otherwise the 5-minute timer would flood logs); systemd timer fires `OnBootSec=1min` + `OnUnitActiveSec=5min` + `Persistent=true`; service is `Type=oneshot` with stdout+stderr to journal; logs go to both `/var/log` and journalctl for redundancy at `user.warning`/`user.notice` priorities; installer self-tests by inducing drift on app 13 and asserting final state. Drift in either side breaks the test before merge. **Why pure SQL guard rather than disabling Coolify auto-update**: Coolify's auto-update brings security patches (the upgrade window also contained CSR + cert refresh activity); turning it off trades one risk for another. The drift guard converts "fragile assumption that 4VD-24 stays applied" into "self-healing within 5 minutes of any future drift" ŌĆö independent of which mechanism caused the flip. The guard log is the canary that catches the same upstream behaviour next time Coolify auto-updates. **Linear** [4VD-37](https://linear.app/4vdataconsulting/issue/4VD-37) closed.

### Removed

- **DocuSeal per-tenant Integration Settings UI + dead validation/icon/imports (4VD-32 Phase A) (`src/components/settings/TenantIntegrationSettings.jsx`)**: `4VD-15` made DocuSeal a single-platform-key install and dropped `loadDocusealConfig`'s legacy `tenant_integrations` lookup, but the per-tenant Settings ŌåÆ Integrations form (DocuSeal API key, base URL, webhook secret, webhook URL display) was still rendered, accepted user input, and silently saved no-op rows. **Removed in this change**: `'docuseal'` from the integration-type Select option list, the `applyIntegrationTypeDefaults` docuseal branch (which prefilled the sslip.io base URL), the submit-handler validation guards (api_key + base_url required), the entire `formData.integration_type === 'docuseal'` form rendering block (~160 lines: API key input, webhook secret input + Generate button, base URL input, copy-to-clipboard webhook URL display), the `FileSignature` lucide icon mapping, and the now-unused `Copy` + `RefreshCw` lucide imports. **Replaced with**: a single-line muted note under the integration-type Select ŌĆö "DocuSeal eSigning is configured platform-wide; contact the operator if you need a different DocuSeal install for this tenant." Webhook signature verification (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js:resolveTenantFromSignature`) continues reading existing `tenant_integrations[type=docuseal,is_active=true]` rows as a legacy fallback path so production webhooks remain green during the migration; full row deletion is deferred to Phase C (operator action ŌĆö see Changed entry below). **Side-finding**: the file had 21 trailing NULL bytes from a prior write that surfaced as a parse error after these edits exposed it (`Parsing error: Unexpected character ' '` on the empty line past `}`); cleaned up to a normal `\n`-terminated EOF. ESLint clean: 0 errors, 4 pre-existing react-refresh warnings unchanged. Frontend Vitest pool was unable to start in the sandbox (Vitest worker thread timeout ŌĆö environment limitation, not a code regression); existing `TenantIntegrationSettings.test.jsx` tests `applyIntegrationTypeDefaults` for `communications_provider` and `calcom` only, neither touches the removed docuseal branch. **In progress towards 4VD-32**.

### Security

- **Supabase advisor remediation across prod (`ehjlenywplgyiahgxkfj`) and staging (`bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`) ŌĆö closes the "security vulnerabilities detected in your projects" advisor email; net 313ŌåÆ~1 prod findings and 119ŌåÆ~2 staging findings (8 migrations applied via MCP, no committed SQL files since Supabase migrations live in the project's migration history, not in `backend/migrations/`)**: Triggered by the Supabase advisor email; pulled `get_advisors(security)` for both projects (prod: 3 ERROR + 310 WARN, staging: 3 ERROR + 116 WARN), categorized into 9 distinct lints, and applied targeted fixes per category. **(1) `function_search_path_mutable` ŌĆö 5 prod / 7 staging functions hardened (migration `sec_fix_function_search_path`)**: `ALTER FUNCTION ... SET search_path = public, pg_temp` on `touch_updated_at`, `billing_set_updated_at`, `billing_events_prevent_modification`, `refresh_person_profile(uuid)`, `get_top_rate_limit_offenders(timestamptz, integer)` (both projects) plus `docuseal_set_updated_at`, `run_dashboard_funnel_refresh_job` (staging only). Chose `public, pg_temp` over `''` because `get_top_rate_limit_offenders` references `rate_limit_violations` unqualified ŌĆö empty search*path would break it. Verified all bodies fully qualify other table refs with `public.` so the change is behavior-neutral. **(2) Dashboard MV API exposure ŌĆö 3 MVs revoked from anon/authenticated on each project (migration `sec_revoke_dashboard_mv_api_access`)**: `REVOKE SELECT ON public.{dashboard_funnel_counts, dashboard_opps_funnel_mv, dashboard_stats_mv} FROM anon, authenticated`. Backend reads via service_role (bypasses RLS) and the dashboard endpoints use the `get_dashboard_bundle`/`get_dashboard_stats` SECURITY DEFINER RPCs, not direct MV reads ŌĆö verified via `routes/reports.js` lines 528, 595. No app impact. **(3) RLS on `ai_campaign_events` + `ai_campaign_targets` ŌĆö 8 policies added across both projects (migration `sec_enable_rls_ai_campaign_events_targets`)**: Both tables had `tenant_id uuid NOT NULL` and 0 rows on prod, 0 on staging ŌĆö safe to lock down. ENABLE RLS + 4 policies per table mirroring the established `accounts`/`contacts`/`leads` pattern: `tenant_id = (SELECT current_tenant_id())` for SELECT/UPDATE/DELETE USING and INSERT/UPDATE WITH CHECK, scoped to `authenticated` only. Closes 4 of the 6 ERROR-level findings (2 per project). **(4) `user_profile_view` SECURITY DEFINER ŌåÆ INVOKER on both projects (migration `sec_user_profile_view_security_invoker`)**: `ALTER VIEW public.user_profile_view SET (security_invoker = on)`. Pre-investigation confirmed (a) backend uses `getSupabaseClient()` from `lib/supabase-db.js` which authenticates with `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` (service_role bypasses RLS ŌĆö no behavior change for `routes/users.js` line 500's `.from('user_profile_view').select(...)`) and (b) underlying tables already have appropriate authenticated-role policies (`users_tenant_select`, `employees_tenant_select`) so direct authenticated reads still resolve to caller's own tenant. The legacy `service_role_only_tenants` policy (`USING (false)` for authenticated) means direct authenticated reads will return NULL `tenant_name` ŌĆö acceptable since no frontend code reads the view directly. Note: prior migration `120_fix_remaining_security_issues.sql` had attempted this fix but never reached prod/staging ŌĆö confirmed via `pg_class.reloptions = null` pre-change. Closes the remaining 2 ERROR-level findings. **(5) `devai_approvals_update_approver` policy tightened (migration `sec_devai_approvals_tighten_update_policy`)**: Pre-existing policy was `USING (true)` ŌĆö any authenticated user could update any approval row. Replaced with: `USING (requested_by = auth.uid() OR approved_by = auth.uid() OR EXISTS(SELECT 1 FROM users WHERE id=auth.uid() AND role IN ('superadmin','admin','owner')))`, with matching `WITH CHECK`. Pattern follows the existing `users_tenant_update` policy on this project (admin override + self-edit). Closes the `rls_policy_always_true` lint on both projects. **(6) `pg_graphql` extension dropped on prod (migration `sec_drop_pg_graphql_unused`)**: This was the dominant prod-side risk ŌĆö 203 of 313 findings (`pg_graphql_anon_table_exposed` ├Ś100 + `pg_graphql_authenticated_table_exposed` ├Ś103) were pg_graphql exposing every public table to both anon and authenticated roles. Verified pg_graphql is unused before dropping: `pg_stat_user_functions` had ZERO calls to `graphql.*`; codebase-wide grep for GraphQL clients (`@apollo/_`, `urql`, `graphql-request`, supabase-js graphql add-on) returned no matches. Staging never had pg_graphql installed which explains why staging had 0 such findings. `DROP EXTENSION IF EXISTS pg_graphql CASCADE`ŌĆö reversible via`CREATE EXTENSION pg_graphql`if a future feature needs it. **(7) SECURITY DEFINER functions ŌĆö EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC + anon + authenticated on ~50 functions per project, whitelisting`current_tenant_id`(migrations`sec_revoke_definer_execute_from_anon_auth`then`sec_revoke_definer_execute_from_public`)**: First migration revoked from anon/authenticated only ŌĆö verification showed effective EXECUTE was still granted because Postgres auto-grants EXECUTE to PUBLIC on every function and PUBLIC inherits to all roles. Re-applied with `REVOKE EXECUTE ... FROM PUBLIC, anon, authenticated`. DO block iterates all `prosecdef=true`public functions excluding`current_tenant_id`(the only one intentionally exposed to authenticated for tenant resolution from JWT). Pre-revoke audit confirmed safety: backend`.rpc()` calls (`leads\_\_\_definer`, `get_dashboard_bundle`, `get_dashboard_stats`, `pep_increment_report_run`, `refresh_dashboard_funnel_counts`, `get_columns_for_table`, `update_phase3_suggestion_telemetry`, etc.) all run through `getSupabaseClient()`which uses service_role and is unaffected; frontend`src/\*\*/_.{js,jsx,ts,tsx}`makes ZERO direct`.rpc()`calls (verified via grep). Triggers continue to fire normally because trigger invocation does not require EXECUTE on the trigger function. Post-fix: prod has 0 anon-executable + 1 auth-executable definer functions (the whitelisted`current*tenant_id`), staging has 1 + 1 (staging's `current_tenant_id`allows anon ŌĆö minor cross-env inconsistency, not security-critical since it returns NULL without a JWT). **(8) Extensions relocated from`public`to`extensions`schema (migrations`sec_move_vector_extension_to_extensions_schema`for prod,`sec_move_extensions_to_extensions_schema_v2`for staging)**: Pre-flight set`search_path = public, extensions`on`service_role`, `authenticated`, and `anon`roles via`ALTER ROLE ... SET search_path`so unqualified extension references continue to resolve after the move. Then`ALTER EXTENSION ... SET SCHEMA extensions`ŌĆö prod:`vector`only (the`ai_memory_chunks.embedding vector(1536)`column had its type OID reference auto-update; ivfflat index also auto-rebound). Staging:`pg_trgm`, `unaccent`, `vector`. **`http`extension cannot be moved**: first staging attempt failed with`ERROR 0A000: extension "http" does not support SET SCHEMA`ŌĆö pgsql-http hardcodes itself to public. Decided to leave`http`in public (1 WARN remains on staging) rather than the destructive workaround of`DROP EXTENSION http CASCADE; CREATE EXTENSION http SCHEMA extensions`which would lose the`public.http_request`and`public.http_response`user tables that have FK-style type dependencies on http types. **(9)`auth_leaked_password_protection`on staging ŌĆö manual follow-up required**: This is an Auth service config flag (HaveIBeenPwned password check), not a database setting, so it can't be toggled via SQL. Doppler`aishacrm/prd_prd`audit showed no`SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN`/ Management API personal access token (only`SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`and`SUPABASE_ADMIN_SECRET`, neither of which authenticates against the Management API). Resolution path documented for the operator: visit `https://supabase.com/dashboard/project/bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj/auth/providers` ŌåÆ Email provider ŌåÆ toggle "Check passwords against HaveIBeenPwned" ON. ~30-second action. To automate in future sessions: create a Supabase personal access token at `https://supabase.com/dashboard/account/tokens` and add it to Doppler as `SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN` so `PATCH /v1/projects/{ref}/config/auth { "password_hibp_enabled": true }` is callable from the sandbox. Prod already has this protection enabled (advisor confirmed). **Verification queries** ran post-migration: prod `ai_campaign*\*`RLS=true,`user_profile_view.reloptions={security_invoker=on}`, `pg_graphql`extension count=0,`vector` schema=`extensions`, definer functions executable by anon=0 / authenticated=1; staging same plus `pg_trgm`/`unaccent`/`vector`in`extensions`, `http`remaining in`public`. **Investigation/diagnostics receipts**: full advisor JSON dumps captured to MCP tool-results files; recommendation rationale and codebase audit (RPC call sites, GraphQL client check, RLS pattern mirroring from `accounts`/`contacts`/`leads`) traced inline above. Net change to advisor counts (estimated, pending re-run of `get_advisors`): prod 313ŌåÆ~1 (residual WARN potentially the staging's `http` doesn't apply to prod, so prod should be near-clean), staging 119ŌåÆ2 (`http`extension_in_public +`auth_leaked_password_protection` until operator toggles).

### Changed

- **DocuSeal moved from Coolify Service template to App-from-Compose, image now pulled from GHCR ŌĆö Service template regen footgun resolved (4VD-27 Phases 2ŌĆō4) (`docuseal-patched/README.md`, Coolify resource `docuseal-staging-app` uuid `amz6bybd0b5f2ha91yxfnywn` on Services server / aishacrm-staging project, OLD Service `Docuseal With Postgres` uuid `vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w` decommissioned)**: 4VD-23's patched DocuSeal image (`docuseal-aishacrm:patched-2026-05-04`) lived only on VPS-2's local Docker daemon and was deployed via a Coolify Service template that regenerated its compose file on every "Redeploy" click ŌĆö silently reverting the image swap and stripping the `coolify` proxy network attachment. Phase 1 (PR #560) shipped the GHCR build pipeline. **Phase 2** (this changeset) created a new Coolify Docker-Compose resource pointing at `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-docuseal-patched:staging-latest`. The new resource was classified by Coolify as a Service (compose pattern matched the built-in `docuseal-with-postgres` template), but it's an inline-compose resource that does NOT regen the compose from a template the way the legacy Service template did ŌĆö it's effectively App-from-Compose with the same Service UI surface. **Phase 3 cutover** (UI-driven, ~10 min, ~60-90s downtime): updated `HOST` env to `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com`, set `FORCE_SSL=false` (Traefik handles HTTPŌåÆHTTPS at the proxy layer; Rails-level FORCE_SSL was breaking the in-container healthcheck because wget follows the 302 redirect to the public domain ŌåÆ Cloudflare ŌåÆ Puma:3000 via TLS handshake ŌåÆ "wrong version number"), changed Docuseal subservice Domains to `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com`, Stop button on OLD Service, Deploy button on new App. Coolify regenerated compose, fired `ConnectProxyToNetworksJob` (attached coolify proxy network), Traefik discovered the new Host rule, Let's Encrypt cert provisioned via HTTP-01 challenge. **Acid test PASSED**: clicked Restart on the new App, all invariants survive ŌĆö image still GHCR, coolify network still attached, patch marker still present (`grep -c AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP /app/app/controllers/submit_form_controller.rb` = 1), HOST/FORCE_SSL preserved, Traefik labels still include `https-...rule=Host('docuseal.aishacrm.com')` + `tls.certresolver=letsencrypt`, external `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com/up` returns HTTP/2 200. **Zero manual intervention required after Restart** ŌĆö this is the proof 4VD-27 was filed for. **Phase 4** (this changeset): docuseal-patched/README.md rewritten to reflect the new architecture (push to GHCR + Coolify Restart instead of edit-compose-on-disk + force-recreate); 4VD-24's stale `build-staging.yml` claim edited in its Linear description to point at 4VD-30 + 4VD-27 as the actual landed solutions; OLD Service deleted via Coolify UI Danger Zone with orphan volumes (`vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w_docuseal-data`, `_postgresql-data`) cleaned up via plink ŌĆö staging data was destructible per project preference, so the cutover fresh-DB approach was acceptable rather than a volume-swap. **Lessons captured to memory** (`coolify_v4_mutation_quirks.md`): Coolify v4 public REST mutation endpoints (`POST /api/v1/applications/dockercompose`, `PATCH /api/v1/services/<uuid>/envs`, `POST /api/v1/services/<uuid>/restart`) hang ~60s and 500 with empty body, but the writes DO land server-side; env values are stored Crypt::encryptString-encrypted in `environment_variables.value` so direct UPDATE breaks the next read (must use Eloquent via `php artisan tinker --execute=` or the UI to mutate); `service_applications.fqdn` is plain text in DB and direct UPDATE works; cutover-class changes (FQDN swap that triggers cert provision) MUST be UI-driven because Coolify's post-deploy hooks (proxy network attachment, Traefik route refresh, cert request) only fire reliably from the Livewire UI flow ŌĆö direct compose recreate via plink misses them. Coolify's daily image cleanup (`docker_cleanup_frequency: 0 0 * * *`) deleted the old local-only image during the Phase 3 attempt window, breaking the rollback path; the GHCR pipeline (Phase 1) eliminates this class of risk because rollback can always pull from registry. **Bonus**: during the rollback attempt, the OLD Service compose was edited to point at the GHCR image too ŌĆö proving the GHCR-pulled image works through both the legacy Service template path AND the new App-from-Compose path. **Verification artifacts**: `scripts/phase2-verify.ps1`, `scripts/verify-http-route.ps1`, `scripts/phase3-v2-verify.ps1` capture the full proof chain (container running healthy on GHCR image, both networks attached, patch marker present, postgres handshake working, SMTP env loaded, Traefik HTTPS+letsencrypt labels live, external CloudflareŌåÆcloudflaredŌåÆTraefik path returning 200). **Closes 4VD-27**.

- **DocuSeal multi-tenant isolation: single platform key + `external_id` tagging, legacy fallback dropped (4VD-15) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-external-id.test.js`, Doppler `aishacrm/{dev,stg,prd}.DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` + `_BASE_URL`)**: The original 4VD-15 spec assumed we needed to provision a separate DocuSeal user per CRM tenant for template/submission isolation, which led to investigating either patching DocuSeal Community's `POST /api/users` endpoint (it doesn't exist ŌĆö verified via live route dump + 404 probe with valid X-Auth-Token while `/api/templates` and `/api/user` return 200) or doing direct PostgreSQL inserts to synthesize User + AccessToken rows. **The simpler architecture, surfaced by Dre noting that templates have an `author_id` and asking "do we need to create a user, or only the author of a template?"**: DocuSeal templates and submissions have an `external_id` field (free-form string, "Identifier of the template in the external system"), the API natively supports `?external_id=X` filtering on `GET /api/templates` (verified via DocuSeal source: `app/controllers/api/templates_controller.rb:95` ŌĆö `templates = templates.where(external_id: params[:external_id]) if params[:external_id].present?`), and PATCH/POST accept `external_id` as a permitted attribute. Live probe 2026-05-06: PATCH set `external_id="test-tenant-zzz"` on template id=1 ŌåÆ HTTP 200, GET filter with that value ŌåÆ returns 1 template, GET filter with bogus value ŌåÆ returns 0 templates. **Implementation** (per Dre's clarification: DocuSeal Community only allows ONE API key, staging is destructible, prod has nothing ŌĆö no legacy fallback needed): (1) `loadDocusealConfig` reads ONLY `process.env.DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` + `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_BASE_URL` (Doppler-injected); legacy per-tenant `tenant_integrations` lookup dropped entirely. Returns `docuseal_platform_not_configured` if either env is missing. (2) `fetchDocusealTemplates` accepts an `externalId` param and appends `&external_id=<id>` (URL-encoded) to the upstream URL; `GET /api/docuseal/templates` route always passes `req.tenant.id` so the cached, returned list is server-side-filtered to that tenant's templates only. (3) `buildDocusealSubmissionPayload` accepts an `externalId` param and includes it on the outbound DocuSeal submission body; `POST /api/docuseal/submissions` route always passes `req.tenant.id` so the submission is tagged from creation. **Tenant isolation enforcement layer**: the platform key has access to ALL tenants' templates, but the CRM proxy's `external_id` filter is THE isolation boundary ŌĆö every list endpoint adds the filter, every read/update/delete (forthcoming in 4VD-28) will validate ownership before mutating. The platform key never leaves Doppler/server env. **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-external-id.test.js`): 13 new covering platform-vs-tenant config selection (5), external_id query-string filter on fetchDocusealTemplates (4: appends when provided, omits when not, URL-encodes special chars, coerces non-string to string), external_id stamp on buildDocusealSubmissionPayload (4: includes/omits/coerces/preserves shape). 96/96 across all 8 docuseal test files now pass. **What's NOT in this commit** (deferred to 4VD-28): new `POST/PATCH/DELETE /api/docuseal/templates/:id` routes for the CRM-native template builder; those will reuse the same external_id stamping and add ownership-validation defense before mutating. **What's NOT in this commit** (deferred to a backfill script): retroactively PATCHing `external_id` onto existing templates and submissions in DocuSeal that pre-date this change; the legacy path's `tenant_integrations` lookup still works as a graceful fallback during the migration window. **Doppler step DONE** in this same change: `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_API_KEY` (the existing admin's X-Auth-Token, prefix `LiJnHh`, sourced from the existing `tenant_integrations.id=ef01b656...` row) and `DOCUSEAL_PLATFORM_BASE_URL=https://docuseal.aishacrm.com` written to `aishacrm/dev`, `aishacrm/stg`, `aishacrm/prd` via Doppler MCP. **Backfill DONE** in this same change: the one existing template (NDA, id=1) PATCHed with `external_id=759a83e8-7340-4482-a586-cd2d049fb0b5` (staging tenant uuid) ŌĆö verified via `GET /api/templates?external_id=<uuid>` returning the tagged template. **Why this beats the original spec**: ~1 day of effort vs ~2 days (would-be DocuSeal patch) or ~1.5 days (would-be direct DB inserts), zero parallel infrastructure to keep in sync, tenant identity stays a CRM concept, future-proof against DocuSeal upgrades because `external_id` is a stable public field rather than a custom controller patch.

### Added

- **CI build pipeline for the patched DocuSeal image ŌĆö publishes to GHCR (4VD-27 Phase 1) (`.github/workflows/build-docuseal-patched.yml`, `backend/__tests__/ci/build-docuseal-patched-coverage.test.js`)**: The patched DocuSeal image (`docuseal-aishacrm:patched-2026-05-04`, the 4VD-23 CSRF-skip on top of upstream `docuseal/docuseal:latest`) lived only on VPS-2's local Docker daemon ŌĆö invisible to anyone else, lost if the daemon's image cache cleared, irreproducible from CI. This workflow promotes it to a registry-hosted artifact at `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-docuseal-patched` so 4VD-27 Phase 2's new Coolify "App from Docker Image" can pull it instead of relying on `pull_policy: never` against a local-only tag. **Trigger**: push to main when `docuseal-patched/**` (or this workflow file) changes, plus `workflow_dispatch` for manual rebuilds when DocuSeal upstream releases a new version (`docuseal_tag` input bumps the `FROM docuseal/docuseal:<tag>` base, `push_latest` input controls whether `:latest` moves with this build for off-cycle prod-only rebuilds). **Tags published per build**: `:staging-latest` (what the new Coolify App will track), `:<short-sha>` (immutable per-build audit trail), `:upstream-<DOCUSEAL_TAG>-<sha>` (couples the patch version to the upstream version it was built against ŌĆö at-a-glance correlation when reviewing image history), and optionally `:latest` (controlled by the workflow input). **Safety net**: post-push verification step pulls the published `:<sha>` tag and `grep -q AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP /app/app/controllers/submit_form_controller.rb` inside the image. Fails the workflow if the marker is missing ŌĆö defends against a successful build that silently drops the patch (e.g., upstream rearranges the file and the sed regex stops matching). Same `grep -q` guard pattern is in the Dockerfile itself for re-run idempotency. **Coverage test** (`build-docuseal-patched-coverage.test.js`, 13 passing tests): mirrors 4VD-30's `staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js` pattern. Pins workflow shape ŌĆö push trigger paths, workflow_dispatch inputs, GHCR registry/image-name slug, build-push-action context+file+build-arg, tag set membership, marker-verification step, Dockerfile cross-reference (the workflow's grep target string must appear in the Dockerfile too). Drift in either side breaks the test before merge. **Build cache**: scoped per-`DOCUSEAL_TAG` so swapping upstream versions invalidates correctly; `mode=max` keeps intermediate layers reusable across runs. Cache key prevents accidental tag-cross-contamination. **Phase 2-4 deferred**: standing up the new Coolify App, cutover, decom of the old Service. Phase 1 lands the publishing infrastructure that all subsequent phases depend on.

- **Staging auto-deploy on push to main ŌĆö replaces the orphaned `build-staging.yml` from 4VD-24 with a slice-cap-safe webhook-only workflow (4VD-30) (`.github/workflows/deploy-staging.yml`, `.github/actions/coolify-deploy/action.yml`, `backend/__tests__/ci/staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js`, `.env`, `scripts/poll-coolify-deploy.ps1`)**: Today's "Send Document button missing on Contact panel" report on `staging-app.aishacrm.com` was actually a stale-bundle issue ŌĆö both `staging-app-fast` and `staging-backend-heavy` were running pre-`d44b9f0f feat(docuseal): eSigning integration MVP` builds. Pushes to `main` had not been auto-deploying staging since commit `3f6ab847 infra(staging): revert GHCR migration` reverted the original `build-staging.yml` in favor of 4VD-24's `system.slice` cap. The slice cap was the right lockup fix, but the CI deploy workflow was a casualty of the revert and never re-landed. **Approach** (4VD-30 Option A): pure webhook-driven, no GHCR side-quest. On push to main, `dorny/paths-filter@v3` computes which of the 4 staging Coolify Applications need a redeploy from per-app path filters that mirror Coolify's own `watch_paths` config (`src/**`, `public/**`, `Dockerfile`, etc. for `staging-app-fast`; `backend/**` + `staging/01-backend-heavy/**` for `staging-backend-heavy`; `braid-mcp-node-server/**` + `staging/04-braid/**` for `staging-braid`; `litellm/**` + `staging/services/litellm/**` for `staging-litellm`). Each affected app fires a job that uses the new `coolify-deploy` composite action: POST `/api/v1/deploy?uuid=<UUID>&force=<bool>` with `Authorization: Bearer ${{ secrets.COOLIFY_DEPLOY_TOKEN }}`, parse `deployment_uuid` from the response, then poll `/api/v1/deployments/<uuid>` every 15s until terminal state (`finished` ŌåÆ exit 0, `failed`/`cancelled` ŌåÆ exit 1, timeout after 40 polls = 10 min). Failure logs include the deployment_uuid for direct Coolify-UI lookup. **Why webhook-only beats GHCR**: Coolify's own builds run inside `coolify.slice` (CPUQuota=100%, MemoryMax=2G per 4VD-24's wiring) so the build CPU is bounded ŌĆö the GHCR migration that 4VD-24 originally tried was reverted because the slice cap solved the real problem. Reintroducing GHCR would mean swapping all 4 staging composes from `build:` ŌåÆ `image:`, GHCR auth, per-Dockerfile multi-stage, and re-validating 4VD-24's `/proc/stat` invariants. Webhook + slice-cap is the simpler proven path. **`workflow_dispatch` shape**: takes optional `apps` input (comma-separated subset like `app-fast,backend-heavy` to force-deploy specific apps regardless of path filter) and `force_rebuild` (passes `force=true` to bust Coolify's build cache). Empty `apps` falls back to path-filter auto-detect. Useful for emergency redeploys without crafting a no-op commit. **Path-filter / Coolify drift guard** (`backend/__tests__/ci/staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js`, 28 passing tests): asserts every `watch_paths` entry from each Coolify Application's API response (snapshotted 2026-05-06 from `GET /api/v1/applications/<uuid>`) appears in the workflow's `dorny/paths-filter` block, every Coolify app has a `deploy-<key>` job, and the composite action contains the POST + poll + terminal-status-check pattern. Drift between Coolify's UI watch_paths and the workflow filter is exactly how the original incident class manifests ŌĆö this test fails the build before it can recur. **Composite action design** (`.github/actions/coolify-deploy/action.yml`): single bash shell step, `set -euo pipefail`, `mktemp` for body capture (so HTTP code and body are reported separately on non-2xx), `jq` to extract `deployment_uuid`. Inputs are `base_url`, `application_uuid`, `application_name` (logging only), `token`, `force_rebuild`, `poll_interval_seconds` (default 15), `poll_max_attempts` (default 40). Reused across all 4 deploy jobs to keep the workflow file reading like a manifest, not a script. **Bonus operational fixes from the diagnosis path**: (a) `.env` had `COOLIFY_BASE_URL=https://appspanel-631819.zap.cloud` ŌĆö that is the Zap hypervisor management panel, NOT Coolify (returns 503 to deploy POSTs). The real Coolify is at `https://deploy.aishacrm.com` per the `aishacrm-vps2` cloudflared tunnel ingress rule. Patched in `.env`; `.env.example` follow-up still pending. (b) `scripts/poll-coolify-deploy.ps1` ŌĆö Windows-side helper that polls a single deployment_uuid until terminal, used during today's manual frontend + backend redeploys before the workflow landed. Reusable for future emergency deploys. **Verification**: 28/28 paths-coverage tests pass via `node --test backend/__tests__/ci/staging-deploy-paths-coverage.test.js`. Both YAML files parse cleanly via `yaml.safe_load` ŌĆö `deploy-staging.yml` has 6 jobs (`changes`, `deploy-app-fast`, `deploy-backend-heavy`, `deploy-braid`, `deploy-litellm`, `summary`) with correct `on: {push: {branches: [main]}, workflow_dispatch: {inputs: {apps, force_rebuild}}}` triggers. **Manual Coolify redeploy already proven end-to-end this session** for both `staging-app-fast` (deployment uuid `wf7c0wxm2dxhg7x5hjtnrjrh`, finished in 5m30s) and `staging-backend-heavy` (deployment uuid `ciu5uavbpdc9ke9kl6sh0nqb`, finished in 6m). The workflow uses the same exact API call shape that worked manually. **Pending validation step (carry-over)**: at least one push to main must demonstrate the workflow firing end-to-end and updating staging without manual intervention; VPS-1 must stay under Zap's 5.5-core cap during the build (per 4VD-24's `/proc/stat` methodology); 4VD-24's stale "build-staging.yml shipped" claim in its description must be edited to reference 4VD-30 as the actual landed solution.

- **VPS-1 lockup root cause + CI image build pipeline for staging ŌĆö eliminates Coolify-side build CPU on the App VPS (`scripts/aishacrm.slice`, `scripts/coolify.slice`, `scripts/sample-vps1-state.sh`, `scripts/inventory-out/diag-vps1-cpu.sh`, `.github/workflows/build-staging.yml`, `staging/01-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/02-app-fast/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/04-braid/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/services/litellm/docker-compose.yml`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-host-cap-coverage.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-ghcr-images.test.js`)**: VPS-1 had been hanging every ~3ŌĆō5 hours during active dev, requiring manual reboots ŌĆö the existing diagnosis ("memory leak in coolify-sentinel" / "tighten aishacrm.slice further") was wrong on both axes. **Investigation**: installed a 1-min CSV sampler on VPS-1 (`/usr/local/bin/sample-vps1-state.sh` ŌåÆ `/var/log/vps1-state.csv`) capturing load1, mem*used, swap, PSI cpu/mem, slice memory + nr_throttled, sentinel/proxy/landing RSS, dockerd RSS, journald RSS. 295 samples over 5 hours, 1 reboot in window (manual, end-of-window). PSI cpu peaked 1.68 during a deploy spike at 20:01 UTC; PSI mem peaked 1.04 for one minute then returned to 0 for the rest of the window. `oom_kill = 0` across every cgroup checked (slice + per-container). `vmstat` showed `id=73 wa=0 st=0` at baseline ŌĆö load avg 8 on a 32-core box is 26% utilization, not saturation. **Cross-referenced** with the Coolify deployment record on VPS-2 via direct Postgres query (`coolify-db`, table `application_deployment_queues` joined to `applications` via `applications.uuid = application_deployment_queues.application_id`): the 20:01 spike was ONE Application redeploying (`staging-app-fast` for commit `0c503f58`), not five; the 187 kernel-veth events are normal kernel network noise for a parallel 2-service deploy with build container + intermediate containers in the lifecycle. **Real root cause** (per Dre's correction "memory was never an issue, it has always been CPU"): Coolify's build phase runs OUTSIDE `aishacrm.slice` (no `cgroup_parent` on Coolify-spawned build containers), so `npm install` + `vite build` can momentarily want 8+ cores. Zap VPS-1 has a hypervisor-enforced 5.5-core sustained CPU cap; when build demand exceeds that, Zap throttles the VM, CPU steal climbs, in-slice services (litellm, backend, braid) miss healthcheck timeouts, sentinel cascades restart attempts, eventually a process hits D-state waiting for hypervisor schedule and the host wedges. The slice cap (`CPUQuota=500%`, `MemoryMax=12G`) was never the binding constraint ŌĆö `nr_throttled` ticked 14 times in 18 minutes on a fresh boot; throttle counter was effectively flat. **Fix package shipped**: (1) `scripts/coolify.slice` ŌĆö sibling slice unit (`CPUQuota=150%`, `MemoryMax=2G`) intended for the Coolify control-plane containers (`coolify-sentinel`, `coolify-proxy`, `aisha-landing-page`) that currently escape `aishacrm.slice`; not yet wired in production, awaits Coolify config UI step. (2) `scripts/sample-vps1-state.sh` + cron entry ŌĆö installed and running on VPS-1 root crontab so the next anomaly comes with full pre-event state. (3) `scripts/inventory-out/diag-vps1-cpu.sh` ŌĆö read-only one-shot diagnostic, safe to re-run. (4) **Watch Paths trim on `staging-backend-heavy`** (applied 2026-05-05 via Coolify Postgres on VPS-2): removed root `package.json` + `package-lock.json` from watch_paths since those are frontend files (backend has its own `backend/package.json` already covered by `backend/**`). After fix: `backend/**, staging/01-backend-heavy/**` only. Pure-frontend dependency bumps no longer redeploy the backend. (5) **Runtime CPU/memory caps applied to all 4 staging Coolify Apps** (2026-05-05 via DB): `limits_cpus=4` and `limits_memory=4g` on `staging-backend-heavy`, `staging-app-fast`, `staging-braid`, `staging-litellm`. Defense-in-depth ŌĆö bounds runtime container, does NOT bound the build container (Coolify v4 schema doesn't expose a per-app build CPU cap, only runtime). Applies on next natural deploy. (6) **CI image build pipeline** (`build-staging.yml`) ŌĆö fires on every push to `main` with per-service path filters (matching Coolify's Watch Paths configuration) using `dorny/paths-filter@v3`, builds backend/frontend/mcp/litellm images via `docker/build-push-action@v5` with GHA cache scope per-service (`<service>-staging` keeps cache separate from prod's tag-driven cache), publishes to GHCR with three tags: `staging-latest` (Coolify tracks), `staging-<sha>` (immutable per-commit, audit trail), `staging-<branch>` (currently equals `staging-main`). Frontend build args mirror prod (`docker-release.yml`) but read staging-specific Supabase + URL values from GitHub vars (`VITE_STAGING_SUPABASE_URL` falls back to `VITE_SUPABASE_URL` if not set). Concurrency group cancels in-flight builds when a new push arrives. (7) **All 4 staging compose files migrated from local `build:` blocks to GHCR `image:` references** (`staging/01-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/02-app-fast/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/04-braid/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/services/litellm/docker-compose.yml`) ŌĆö Coolify now pulls pre-built images instead of compiling on VPS-1, eliminating the build CPU spike entirely. Frontend's runtime entrypoint (`frontend-entrypoint.sh`) still populates `env-config.js` from container env at startup so a single image serves both prod and staging via runtime config. (8) **Tests** (`backend/__tests__/routes/staging-host-cap-coverage.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-ghcr-images.test.js`): regression contracts pinning that staging composes (a) bind every service to `cgroup_parent: aishacrm.slice`, (b) reference `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-{backend,frontend,mcp,litellm}:staging-latest` images, (c) contain no local `build:` blocks. Plus a workflow-shape test that fails if `build-staging.yml` is missing the on-main trigger, the `staging-latest` tag, the per-SHA tag, or any of the four service matrix entries. **Phase 2 (shipped same changeset)**: (a) **`coolify.slice` is now wired and live on VPS-1 as of 2026-05-06**: investigation against Coolify's data model confirmed `coolify-sentinel`, `coolify-proxy` are server-level Coolify infra (not user resources, not in `applications`/`services`/`service_applications`/`standalone_dockers` tables) and `aisha-landing-page` is also outside Coolify entirely (manual `docker run` or manual compose). None has a per-resource UI surface for `cgroup_parent`. The viable wiring path was daemon-level: added `"cgroup-parent": "coolify.slice"` to `/etc/docker/daemon.json` on VPS-1 (preserved existing `log-driver`, `log-opts`, `default-address-pools` keys; backup at `/etc/docker/daemon.json.bak.<ts>`), `systemctl restart docker` (~25s container bounce; all 12 containers came back healthy because we'd already disabled `auto_deploy_enabled` so Coolify didn't auto-redeploy mid-bounce). Verified post-restart via `/proc/<pid>/cgroup` (the kernel ground truth ŌĆö `docker inspect HostConfig.CgroupParent` returns `<none>` for daemon-default-cgroup containers and is misleading): `coolify-sentinel` ŌåÆ `coolify.slice/docker-7030bbŌĆ”scope`, `coolify-proxy` ŌåÆ `coolify.slice/docker-1d633eŌĆ”scope`, `aisha-landing-page` ŌåÆ `coolify.slice/docker-ffa06cŌĆ”scope`. All 9 AiSHA containers stayed in `aishacrm.slice/...` (unaffected; explicit `cgroup_parent` in their compose overrides the daemon default). Future Coolify-spawned helper containers (build, healthcheck wrappers, etc.) will inherit `coolify.slice` cap (1.5 cores sustained, 2 GB max) instead of being unbounded ŌĆö this was the actual lockup driver and is now bounded. (b) **Post-build deploy trigger from CI to Coolify is wired**: new `deploy` job in `build-staging.yml` runs after `build` matrix completes successfully, reads the `changes` job's per-service flags, and calls `POST https://deploy.aishacrm.com/api/v1/deploy?uuid=<app-uuid>&force=false` for each Coolify Application whose source actually changed. UUIDs are env-vars in the workflow (sourced from Coolify v4 API): `staging-backend-heavy=d24ro1fqm0zyl7pd72g6snd2`, `staging-app-fast=di7ko49ikfd2mz8yh0q7id8q`, `staging-braid=tw8zmua5jyzwnhh1oxw15kkm`, `staging-litellm=zsy5fsbw9hccxvoznkbpy1il`. **Backend-image rebuild fans out to TWO Coolify apps** because `staging-app-fast` contains both `frontend` (frontend image) AND `aisha-comms` (backend image with a different `command:`); when the backend image changes, both apps need to pull. The deploy step de-duplicates so a commit that touches both backend and frontend doesn't double-fire `staging-app-fast`. 5-second sleep between trigger calls keeps the burst from saturating VPS-1 with simultaneous pulls; Coolify processes the deploys async on its end. Required GitHub repo secret: `COOLIFY_DEPLOY_TOKEN` (Coolify v4 API token, scoped to deploy permissions). The workflow's first step verifies the secret is set and fails with an explicit error pointing at the GitHub Settings URL if missing. (c) **`auto_deploy_enabled` disabled on all 4 staging apps via Coolify Postgres**: the column lives in `application_settings.is_auto_deploy_enabled` (joined to `applications.id` via `application_id`), not on `applications` directly ŌĆö Coolify v4 schema split. Set to `false` for application_ids 12, 13, 15, 19. Now Coolify only deploys when the CI workflow calls its webhook; the previous race window (Coolify pulls `:staging-latest` on git-push \_before* CI has finished building and pushing the new image) is closed. Manual redeploys via the Coolify UI still work ŌĆö only git-push triggering is disabled. **Memory hygiene**: removed the `coolify-sentinel auto-kill regex` follow-up from the immediate plan after Dre clarified CPU-not-memory framing ŌĆö the `find.*\.next` match in `/usr/local/bin/stress-event-logger.sh`'s `check_runaway_processes` is still a footgun that can shoot down legitimate Vite builds mid-deploy and remains queued.

- **DocuSeal Community CSRF skip patch for `/s/:slug` PUT ŌĆö unblocks white-label embedded signing (4VD-23) (`docuseal-patched/Dockerfile`, `docuseal-patched/README.md`)**: 4VD-7 staging test confirmed that the iframe field-save POST returns HTTP 422 even with same-site framing (`staging-app.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ docuseal.aishacrm.com`). Investigation against the DocuSeal source on GitHub identified the root cause as Rails `ActionController::InvalidAuthenticityToken` thrown by `protect_from_forgery` in `SubmitFormController#update`, surfaced as bare `{"status":422}` via the global `ErrorsController`. Cookie-partitioning under SameSite/CHIPS prevents the embedded iframe's session cookie from matching the session that signed the embedded `authenticity_token`, regardless of eTLD+1. Hypotheses ruled out: submitter not "primed" (`POST /api/submitter_form_views` already sets `opened_at`), 2FA/email-verify (defaults off), field validation (returns JSON with an `error` key, not bare 422). The slug in `/s/:slug` is itself an unguessable per-submitter UUID ŌĆö it already acts as a capability token, so removing CSRF on this single action does not meaningfully reduce security (CSRF only mattered if you assumed the sender's session was the access control, and it isn't). DocuSeal Pro's `<docuseal-form>` web component + `/embed/forms` API solves the same problem differently with proper CORS, but Community doesn't have it. **Fix**: child Dockerfile that wraps upstream `docusealco/docuseal:<TAG>` and applies one idempotent sed patch ŌĆö `skip_before_action :verify_authenticity_token, only: :update` on `SubmitFormController`, marked with `# AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP` for audit. Build with `docker build --build-arg DOCUSEAL_TAG=<version> -t docuseal-aishacrm:patched-<date> .`. Deploy via Coolify by switching the docuseal app's image source to the patched tag. Maintenance: ~5 min per upstream release ŌĆö bump `DOCUSEAL_TAG`, rebuild, redeploy. The sed is guarded so re-running when upstream eventually adds the line natively is a no-op rather than a break. **Staging deploy completed 2026-05-05**: image built on VPS-2 from `docuseal/docuseal:latest` (NOTE: Docker Hub repo is `docuseal/docuseal`, not `docusealco/docuseal` ŌĆö Dockerfile and README corrected), tagged `docuseal-aishacrm:patched-2026-05-04`, swapped into the running container by editing `/data/coolify/services/vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w/docker-compose.yml` in place (added `pull_policy: never`, marker comment `# AISHACRM_4VD23`) and running `docker compose up -d --no-deps --force-recreate docuseal`. Container reports healthy, public endpoint serves HTTP 200 in ~230 ms, the `# AISHACRM_4VD23_CSRF_SKIP` marker grep returns the expected three lines from the live container. **Coolify caveat documented in `docuseal-patched/README.md`**: DocuSeal on VPS-2 is a Coolify Service (template-managed), so any "Redeploy" click in the Coolify UI regenerates the compose file from the upstream template and reverts the patched image to `docuseal/docuseal:latest`. After any Coolify-driven redeploy the swap must be re-applied. Long-term fix is to migrate the resource from a Coolify "Service" to an "App from Docker Image" so the image becomes user-configurable; queued as a follow-up. **End-to-end smoke test on `staging-app.aishacrm.com` PASSED 2026-05-05**: recipient signed via the iframed flow, NEXT and COMPLETE buttons advanced cleanly, "Document has been signed!" rendered. Network probe of `PUT /s/<slug>` returned HTTP 200 (was 422 pre-patch). Direct verification of the patched controller in the live container shows the marker comment + `skip_before_action :verify_authenticity_token, only: :update`. **Closes 4VD-23**.

- **DocuSeal embedded signing ŌĆö `allow-downloads` added to iframe sandbox so the post-signing DOWNLOAD button on the completion screen actually saves the PDF (`src/pages/SignPage.jsx`)**: Modern browsers silently block iframe-initiated downloads unless the sandbox attribute explicitly lists `allow-downloads`. The original token list omitted it (the comment incorrectly attributed download behaviour to `allow-popups`, which only governs popup window navigation). Recipients clicking DOWNLOAD on DocuSeal's "Document has been signed!" view experienced a no-op ŌĆö no error toast, no download, just nothing. Fixed by appending `allow-downloads` to the existing token list and rewriting the inline comment to document the staging-bug rationale so a future "let's tighten the sandbox" PR has to consciously override the token. Verified live on staging post-redeploy.

- **DocuSeal webhook auth model switched from HMAC-SHA256 to static-secret-equality to match DocuSeal Community's actual outbound behaviour (4VD-7 follow-up) (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook.test.js`)**: Investigation against the running `/app/app/jobs/send_*_webhook_request_job.rb` files in the patched DocuSeal Community container revealed that `webhook_url.secret` is a JSON hash spread as static HTTP headers on every outbound webhook (`**webhook_url.secret.to_h`) ŌĆö it is NOT an HMAC. The "Webhook Secret" dialog in DocuSeal admin is literally a Key + Value form for adding a custom request header. Our previous `verifyDocusealSignature` computed `HMAC-SHA256(rawBody, secret)` against the inbound header, which would never match Community's static-header dispatch. Net effect: every webhook returned 401 `invalid_signature`, no submission ever flipped from `sent` ŌåÆ `completed` in the CRM, even though signing worked end-to-end on the recipient side. **Fix**: detect mode by header prefix ŌĆö `sha256=<hex>` triggers HMAC verification (kept for DocuSeal Pro / future deployments), plain hex triggers constant-time string equality against the stored `webhook_secret`. Operator-side config: in DocuSeal admin ŌåÆ Webhooks ŌåÆ Add Secret, set `Key=X-Docuseal-Signature, Value=<the same 64-char hex stored on tenant_integrations.api_credentials.webhook_secret>`. Documented inline at the top of the verify function so the next maintainer doesn't relitigate. **Security note**: the slug in `/s/:slug` is itself a per-submitter UUID capability token; a leaked secret would let an attacker forge completion events for that one tenant but couldn't enumerate other tenants' submissions, and webhook payload integrity is bounded by DocuSeal's outbound state. Acceptable for Community deployments; tighter HMAC is automatic if DocuSeal Pro is later adopted. **Tests**: 8 new (5 static-secret mode + 3 HMAC mode) covering equal/unequal/empty-header/null-secret/length-mismatch/malformed-hex paths. 24/24 in `__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook.test.js` pass.

- **DocuSeal admin webhook URL field silently reverted to `https://example.com` after the secret dialog SUBMIT (operational fix, not code)**: After configuring the URL field with `https://staging-api.aishacrm.com/api/webhooks/docuseal`, opening "ADD SECRET", and clicking SUBMIT in the dialog, the URL field reset to the placeholder default and the parent SAVE button was needed separately to persist the URL. Decryption of the stored `WebhookUrl` row via Rails console showed the URL field saved as `example.com`, so DocuSeal was POSTing to `example.com` and getting back the IANA placeholder HTML with HTTP 405 ŌĆö which DocuSeal logged as a webhook delivery failure. Operator re-pasted the URL and clicked SAVE; webhooks now flow correctly. Documented as a 4VD-7 setup gotcha ŌĆö first-run DocuSeal admin webhook setup must (a) paste URL ŌåÆ SAVE, (b) ADD SECRET ŌåÆ SUBMIT, (c) re-verify URL is still set, (d) SAVE again. Worth a follow-up Linear note to either patch DocuSeal upstream or document this in CARE setup docs.

- **DocuSeal lifecycle events ŌĆö handle the full DocuSeal Community event surface, including the renamed `form.declined` and the previously unmapped `form.started` (4VD-9) (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-events.test.js`)**: The MVP `EVENT_MAP` only covered `form.viewed`, `form.completed`, `submission.completed`, `submission.declined`, `submission.expired`. Two gaps surfaced during 4VD-7 verification: (1) DocuSeal Community renamed `submission.declined` ŌåÆ `form.declined` somewhere between MVP rollout and 2026-05 ŌĆö the `WebhookUrl::EVENTS` constant in the patched container's source confirmed this; the old name may still be sent by older installs, so the mapping needs to support both. (2) `form.started` fires when a recipient first opens the signing form ŌĆö same lifecycle meaning as `form.viewed`, but on some DocuSeal installs only `started` fires, never `viewed`. **Fix**: extended `EVENT_MAP` to map `form.started` ŌåÆ identical shape to `form.viewed` (status=viewed, activity=document_viewed, viewed_at timestamp; the existing 1-hour dedupe in `createActivity` collapses any duplicate activity if both fire), and `form.declined` ŌåÆ identical shape to `submission.declined` (status=declined, activity=document_declined). Older installs sending `submission.declined` keep working unchanged. The full DocuSeal v1.10+ webhook event list is documented inline above `EVENT_MAP` so the next maintainer knows which events are intentionally unmapped (`submission.created` overlaps with our own send-route INSERT; `submission.archived`/`template.*` are operational events the CRM doesn't act on; their `last_event_id` still updates so a future revision can pick them up idempotently). **Tests**: 18 new in `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-events.test.js` covering EVENT_MAP coverage of all 7 lifecycle events, mapping shape contracts, view-equivalent identity (form.viewed === form.started), decline-rename identity (form.declined === submission.declined), forward progressions, regression rejections, and unknown-status handling. `EVENT_MAP`, `STATUS_RANK`, `canTransition` exported. Full docuseal test surface: 74/74 across 5 files. **Operator-side requirement**: in DocuSeal admin ŌåÆ Webhooks, ensure all 7 events are checked: `form.viewed`, `form.started`, `form.completed`, `form.declined`, `submission.completed`, `submission.declined` (legacy), `submission.expired`. The 7-event checklist is now a documented step alongside the existing webhook URL + secret config.

- **DocuSeal Templates dropdown ŌĆö replaces the template-id paste field in SendDocumentDialog with a tenant-isolated picker (4VD-8) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-templates.test.js`, `src/components/docuseal/SendDocumentDialog.jsx`)**: SendDocumentDialog asked the user to paste a numeric template_id copied from DocuSeal admin ŌĆö fine for an MVP smoke test, but unworkable for end users who will be picking "Independent Contractor Agreement" or "NDA ŌĆö Mutual" by name. **Backend route**: new `GET /api/docuseal/templates` proxies to DocuSeal's `GET /api/templates?limit=200` using the per-tenant API key from `tenant_integrations.api_credentials.api_key` (looked up via the existing `loadDocusealConfig` helper that's already keyed by `req.tenant.id`). **Tenant isolation invariant**: the in-process cache is a `Map<tenantId, {data, expiresAt}>` keyed by `tenant_id` ONLY ŌĆö never shared across tenants. Two unit tests pin this directly: (1) `fetchDocusealTemplates` sends exactly one request with the supplied apiKey and never falls back to another tenant's key, (2) two sequential calls with different apiKeys return independent results, with no helper-level memoization. A future "let's add a global cache for performance" PR has to actively override these tests rather than silently regress isolation. The cache TTL is 60s; bypass via `?refresh=1`. **Helpers**: `normalizeDocusealTemplate(t)` coerces `id` to string for stable React keys, falls back to "Template <id>" when name is missing, returns null for malformed records. `fetchDocusealTemplates({apiKey, baseUrl, fetchImpl})` handles both `{data: [...]}` envelope and bare-array responses, filters out `archived_at != null`, sorts alphabetically by name. Both exported. **Frontend**: SendDocumentDialog now has three template-input modes ŌĆö `loading` (initial fetch), `dropdown` (shadcn `<Select>` populated from response), and `paste` (graceful fallback when fetch fails or returns empty). The paste mode preserves the MVP behaviour exactly so an upstream config error never leaves the dialog unusable. A "Refresh" button next to the dropdown bypasses the per-tenant cache via `?refresh=1`. Empty-list state shows a tenant-friendly hint ("No templates found in DocuSeal for this tenant. Create one in DocuSeal admin, then click Refresh") with an inline escape to paste mode. Error states include the upstream reason so support diagnostics surface to the user without log digging. **Tests**: 14 new in `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-templates.test.js` (5 normalize + 7 fetch + 2 isolation invariant). 56/56 across the 4 docuseal test files now pass.

- **DocuSeal "View signed PDF" link in the Document Signatures workflow card now points at the durable Supabase Storage mirror, not DocuSeal's hosted URL (4VD-7 / 4VD-13 follow-up) (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-mirror-url.test.js`, `src/components/contacts/ContactDetailPanel.jsx`)**: The Documents paperclip section and Document Management page both already rendered the Supabase Storage URL (per the migration 160 / webhook step 8b mirror), but the Contact panel's Document Signatures workflow card kept rendering DocuSeal's hosted `signed_document_url`. Three different surfaces showing the same logical PDF, two different durability profiles ŌĆö if DocuSeal ever lost its volume on VPS-2, the workflow card link would break while the other two survived. Added `resolveSupabaseStorageUrl(supabase, bucket, path)` (mirrors the public-URL-then-7-day-signed-URL pattern from `routes/storage.js`) and `enrichSubmissionsWithMirrorUrl(supabase, rows, opts)`, wired into `GET /api/docuseal/submissions` so the response includes a `mirror_url` field on each row that has `supabase_storage_path` populated. Frontend `ContactDetailPanel.jsx` precedence is now `signedHref = s.mirror_url || s.signed_document_url` ŌĆö graceful fallback for old submissions whose mirror hasn't run yet. Both helpers exported from `backend/routes/docuseal.js` for unit testing; 11 new tests in `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-mirror-url.test.js` cover empty-path / public-URL / signed-URL fallback / signed-url error / storage-client throws / mixed list ordering / custom bucket. Full docuseal test surface: 42/42 across 3 files.

- **Generated Supabase TS types + `// @ts-check` on docuseal routes ŌĆö 4VD-7 Bug 4 class is now a compile-time error (4VD-16) (`backend/types/database.types.ts`, `backend/types/branding.types.ts`, `backend/lib/logger.d.ts`, `backend/lib/supabaseFactory.js`, `backend/lib/supabase-db.js`, `backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/routes/public-docuseal.js`, `backend/scripts/generate-database-types.mjs`, `backend/tsconfig.json`, `package.json`)**: 4VD-7's smoke test exposed that `.select(...)` strings against Supabase were unchecked literals ŌĆö Bug 4 was a route asking for `tenant.logo_url` (which doesn't exist; the field lives in `branding_settings` jsonb) and getting silently nulled out by `.maybeSingle()`. Closes that gap. **Generated types**: ran `mcp__supabase__generate_typescript_types` against the dev branch (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`), wrote 277KB to `backend/types/database.types.ts` (model classes + Json union for jsonb columns + enum literals). Re-runnable via `npm run db:types` which wraps `npx supabase gen types typescript --project-id nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj` (requires `supabase login` once). **Typed client**: `getSupabaseDB()`, `getSupabaseAdmin()`, `getSupabaseClient()` all return `SupabaseClient<Database>` via JSDoc `@type` annotations ŌĆö no source rewrite to TS needed; the routes stay JS but get TS diagnostics through `// @ts-check`. **Branding shape**: added `backend/types/branding.types.ts` exporting `TenantBranding` + `DocusealSubmissionMetadata` so reads off `branding_settings` and `metadata` jsonb columns are typed at the cast site (`(row.branding_settings ?? {}) as TenantBranding`) ŌĆö typos in field names still surface, runtime missingness is explicit. **Logger shim**: added `backend/lib/logger.d.ts` (sibling to `logger.js`) so the codebase's `logger.warn(msg, structuredFields)` shape is accepted by tsc without rewriting all 28 route files. **Proof of catch**: temporarily reverting `docuseal.js` to its pre-fix `.select('logo_url, primary_color, ...')` produces `error TS2339: Property 'slug' does not exist on type 'SelectQueryError<"column \\'logo_url\\' does not exist on \\'tenant\\'.">'` ŌĆö supabase-js's generic narrows the entire row to a typed error literal naming the bad column. Bug 4 would have failed `npm run typecheck:backend` before merge. **Tooling**: `backend/tsconfig.json` updated with `allowJs/checkJs/noEmit/skipLibCheck`; `npm run typecheck:backend` runs `tsc --noEmit -p backend/tsconfig.json`. **Scope of `@ts-check`**: only `routes/docuseal.js` + `routes/public-docuseal.js` annotated as proof points; remaining 26 route files queued for follow-up sweep on 4VD-16 (the typecheck pass on the docuseal routes specifically is what counts as "implemented" ŌĆö the rest is a mechanical roll-out). **Migration runbook update**: every `apply_migration` must now be followed by `npm run db:types` and a commit of the regenerated `database.types.ts`. Memory file updated.

- **DocuSeal white-label embedded signing ŌĆö recipients land on a tenant-branded, CRM-hosted page; no DocuSeal branding visible (4VD-7) (`backend/migrations/161_tenant_slug.sql`, `backend/routes/tenants.js`, `backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/routes/public-docuseal.js`, `backend/lib/sendTenantEmail.js`, `backend/lib/docusealSignRequestEmail.js`, `backend/server.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/tenants-slug.test.js`, `backend/__tests__/lib/docusealSignRequestEmail.test.js`, `src/pages/SignPage.jsx`, `src/pages/index.jsx`, `src/components/settings/BrandingSettings.jsx`, `src/components/docuseal/SendDocumentDialog.jsx`, `cloudflare-workers/docuseal-iframe-allowlist/`)**: Strategic differentiator vs GoHighLevel. Pre-change: every DocuSeal recipient saw a `docuseal.aishacrm.com`-hosted signing page with DocuSeal's logo and "Powered by DocuSeal" footer ŌĆö the tenant's brand was nowhere to be seen. Post-change: recipients land on a CRM-served page at `https://app.aishacrm.com/sign/<tenant-slug>/<submission-uuid>` showing the tenant's logo and brand colors as page chrome, with DocuSeal's `<docuseal-form>` web component embedded inline for the actual signing UI. **Schema gap closed**: tenants didn't have a URL-safe identifier; Migration 161 adds `tenant.slug TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL` with CHECK `^[a-z0-9](-?[a-z0-9])+$` and length 2..64, backfilled from `tenant.name` via SQL slugify (lowercase, non-alphanumeric ŌåÆ hyphen, collision suffix). Applied to dev (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`) and staging (`bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`); will be applied to prod when 4VD-7 ships there. **Public route**: `GET /api/public/docuseal/sign/:slug/:token` (no auth middleware ŌĆö recipients are not CRM users; the slug+token pair gates access via 404-on-mismatch). Returns embed_src + tenant branding, supports a graceful fallback for legacy submissions without an embed_src. **Tenant slug helpers** (`isValidTenantSlug`, `slugifyTenantName`) exported from `routes/tenants.js` and unit-tested (12 tests). **POST /api/docuseal/submissions** updated: now calls DocuSeal with `send_email: false`, captures the per-submitter `embed_src`, stores it on `docuseal_submissions.metadata.embed_src`, builds the white-label URL via `${FRONTEND_URL}/sign/<slug>/<id>`, and queues a tenant-branded HTML+text email through a new `sendTenantEmail` helper that picks the first active `communications_provider` integration for the tenant (any mailbox; no inbox-pairing required). **Email template** is a pure function (`buildDocusealSignRequestEmail`) with HTML escaping and CSS-injection guards; 9 unit tests cover XSS/injection paths. **Graceful degradation**: if no SMTP provider is configured for the tenant, the route still returns 201 with a `signing_url` field so the user can copy/paste the link manually. **Frontend**: new `/sign/:slug/:token` route (outside Layout ŌĆö no nav, no auth), renders DocuSeal's web component dynamically loaded from CDN. `BrandingSettings.jsx` gains a slug input with live URL preview and inline format validation. `SendDocumentDialog.jsx` shows a "Copy link" toast action when email send falls back. **Tests**: 35/35 across the 3 webhook/slug/email files. **Iframe header rewrite ŌĆö Cloudflare Worker** (`cloudflare-workers/docuseal-iframe-allowlist/`): DocuSeal Community ships `X-Frame-Options: SAMEORIGIN` baked into Rails with no env to disable. A blanket Cloudflare Transform Rule strip would lose clickjacking protection for every visitor; instead, the new Worker (deployed to `docuseal.aishacrm.com/*`) detects whether the request originates from an allowlisted CRM origin (`app.aishacrm.com`, `staging-app.aishacrm.com`, `localhost:4000`, `localhost:5173`) via `Origin` (with `Sec-Fetch-Site=cross-site` + `Referer` fallback) and ONLY THEN rewrites the response: removes `X-Frame-Options`, replaces `Content-Security-Policy`'s `frame-ancestors` with our allowlist while preserving other CSP directives. Direct visits and unrelated framers still see DocuSeal's original headers. 13 unit tests against the pure helpers (`detectAllowlistedOrigin`, `rewriteCsp`); end-to-end requires deploy + browser test. Deploy via `cd cloudflare-workers/docuseal-iframe-allowlist && npx wrangler@latest deploy`. **Out of scope (per Linear issue)**: per-tenant custom domains (CNAME + wildcard cert), multi-recipient/sequential signing, white-label completion email. Closes 4VD-7. Also closes 4VD-21 (origin-allowlist hardening) since it shipped together rather than as a follow-up.
