- **DocuSeal signed PDFs mirrored into Supabase Storage `tenant-assets` bucket on `submission.completed` for durability (4VD-13) (`backend/migrations/160_docuseal_supabase_storage_path.sql`, `backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook.test.js`)**: Until this change, signed PDFs lived ONLY inside DocuSeal's Docker volume on VPS-2 ŌĆö `docuseal_submissions.signed_document_url` and `documents.file_url` both pointed at DocuSeal-hosted URLs. Volume loss = total loss of every signed contract with no recovery path. Closes the durability gap before the first paying customer signs anything. **Implementation**: (1) Migration 160 adds nullable `docuseal_submissions.supabase_storage_path TEXT` (additive, idempotent, applied to dev branch `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj` and staging parent `bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj` via `apply_migration`). (2) Webhook step 8c added (after the documents-table mirror): on `submission.completed`, fetch the signed PDF from `signed_document_url` (with X-Auth-Token from the tenant's DocuSeal API key, 30s timeout via AbortController), upload to `tenant-assets` at `uploads/{tenant_id}/docuseal/{submission_id}_{sanitized_template}.pdf` (upsert=true so retries are safe), persist the path on `docuseal_submissions.supabase_storage_path`, then flip `documents.file_url` to the resulting Supabase Storage public URL (or 7-day signed URL if the bucket is private ŌĆö same fallback pattern as `routes/storage.js`). (3) Idempotency: `supabase_storage_path IS NULL` guard wraps the entire mirror block, so webhook replays after a successful mirror are no-ops. (4) Failure handling: the mirror is wrapped in try/catch and any error is logged at `warn` and swallowed ŌĆö webhook still returns 200, the activity row still lands, and the DocuSeal-hosted URL remains valid for immediate access; a future event or backfill job can re-attempt. **Mirror logic extracted as testable helpers** (`sanitizeTemplateName`, `buildDocusealStorageKey`, `fetchDocusealSignedPdf`, `mirrorSignedPdfToStorage`) so the new test file (`backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-webhook.test.js`, 16 tests, all pass) can exercise happy path + four failure modes (missing `signed_document_url`, storage upload error, DB pointer update error, documents.file_url flip error) without needing a live backend or Supabase project ŌĆö unlike the existing webhook integration tests which require a running server. **Backfill of pre-existing dev/staging signed submissions deliberately skipped per the issue's "optional" note** ŌĆö no production data exists yet. Architecture decision: mirror to Supabase Storage (not R2) per `R2_ARTIFACT_STORAGE.md` boundary ŌĆö `tenant-assets` is for user-uploaded files, R2 `aishacrm-artifacts` is reserved for AI-generated artifacts (chat transcripts, agent traces). `UniversalDetailPanel.jsx` already handles Supabase Storage URLs, so no frontend change needed. Linear: 4VD-13 (status: In Progress).

- **DocuSeal signed PDFs mirror into the generic `documents` table on completion (`backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`)**: When `submission.completed` fires, the webhook now ALSO inserts a row into `documents` with `related_type`/`related_id` matching the entity, `file_url=signed_document_url`, `file_type='application/pdf'`, and `metadata.source='docuseal'` for traceability. The "Documents" paperclip section in `UniversalDetailPanel.jsx` then surfaces signed contracts inline alongside any other attached files ŌĆö no UI duplication, no Lead/Account panel rework needed. Idempotent via metadata.docuseal_submission_id existence check.

- **DocuSeal eSigning integration MVP ŌĆö send documents for signature from contact panels (`backend/migrations/159_docuseal_integration.sql`, `backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/routes/docuseal-webhook.js`, `src/components/docuseal/SendDocumentDialog.jsx`, `src/components/contacts/ContactDetailPanel.jsx`, `src/components/settings/TenantIntegrationSettings.jsx`, `backend/server.js`)**: DocuSeal was deployed on VPS-2 since 2026-05-01 (Coolify-managed, container `docuseal-vv17acequgm4r0g5ek0fvu6w`, sslip.io URL) but had zero CRM integration code. Implemented end-to-end MVP: user clicks "Send Document" on a contact ŌåÆ dialog with template_id paste + recipient email ŌåÆ backend `POST /api/docuseal/submissions` creates DocuSeal submission, inserts tracking row in `docuseal_submissions`, logs `document_sent` activity ŌåÆ DocuSeal emails the recipient ŌåÆ recipient signs ŌåÆ DocuSeal webhook fires `submission.completed` to `POST /api/webhooks/docuseal` ŌåÆ handler verifies HMAC against tenant's webhook_secret in `tenant_integrations`, updates submission status to `completed`, stores `signed_document_url`, logs `document_completed` activity ŌåÆ contact panel's "Document signatures" section reflects status (polls every 30s). **Architecture**: shared DocuSeal instance for all CRM tenants, per-tenant API keys + webhook secrets stored in `tenant_integrations` (no schema change there), single new table `docuseal_submissions` with polymorphic `(related_to, related_id)` pointer matching the `activities` pattern. Webhook idempotency via `last_event_id` column; status transition guard prevents `completed ŌåÆ viewed` regressions; viewed events deduped within 1h. **Cut from MVP, queued for follow-ups (tasks #53+)**: templates dropdown (currently template_id paste-from-DocuSeal), Lead/Account/Opportunity panel parity (trivial copy-paste), signed-PDF streaming proxy (currently direct DocuSeal URL), Braid `docuseal.braid` tool, Cloudflare tunnel route `docuseal.aishacrm.com` (currently sslip.io URL), declined/expired event handling, auto-send on lead conversion. **To finish setup**: create DocuSeal admin account at the sslip.io URL, generate API key, create one template, configure in CRM via Settings ŌåÆ Integrations ŌåÆ DocuSeal type, paste the displayed webhook URL into DocuSeal admin webhook settings.

### Fixed

- **DocuSeal Send Document ŌĆö four bugs surfaced during 4VD-7 local smoke test against `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com` (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-submission-payload.test.js`)**: Both manifested as the frontend showing "DocuSeal send failed" with HTTP 400 from `POST /api/docuseal/submissions`. The CRM proxies any 4xx from DocuSeal as a single 400 with `{error: 'docuseal_send_failed', status, body}`, so the actual cause was only visible in the response payload (network tab) ŌĆö not in the docker backend logs, where pino's `logger.warn('[Docuseal] Send failed', { status, body })` rendered the message line but suppressed the structured fields, making first-pass diagnosis dead-end. **Bug 1 ŌĆö stale API key (401 from DocuSeal)**: The DocuSeal admin API token had been rotated in DocuSeal admin UI but the new value was never re-pasted into `tenant_integrations.api_credentials.api_key` for tenant `759a83e8-7340-4482-a586-cd2d049fb0b5` (Dev Local Tenant). DocuSeal's X-Auth-Token check returned 401 "Not authenticated" ŌåÆ CRM proxied as 400 `docuseal_send_failed`. **Fix**: validated the rotated key directly against `https://docuseal.aishacrm.com/api/templates` (HTTP 200, returned template id 1), then `UPDATE tenant_integrations SET api_credentials = jsonb_set(api_credentials, '{api_key}', ...)` on the dev branch (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`). No code change ŌĆö operational fix. **Bug 2 ŌĆö `message must be a Object` (422 from DocuSeal)**: After the key was fixed, DocuSeal returned HTTP 422 with body `{"error":"message must be a Object"}`. Root cause: the route was forwarding `SendDocumentDialog`'s plain-string `message` field directly into the DocuSeal payload, but DocuSeal's `POST /api/submissions` accepts `message` only as `{subject, body}` Object. Worse, with the 4VD-7 white-label change `send_email: false`, DocuSeal sends no email itself ŌĆö its `message` field is a no-op. The user-typed dialog message was already correctly flowing into our branded email via `buildDocusealSignRequestEmail`; the second use site was dead code that just crashed DocuSeal. **Fix**: extracted `buildDocusealSubmissionPayload({template_id, recipient_email, recipient_name})` as a pure exported helper that returns exactly `{template_id, send_email: false, submitters: [{email, [name]}]}` ŌĆö no `message` field, no `undefined`-valued keys. Inline comment in the route documents why `message` is omitted so a future "let's also pass message to DocuSeal" PR has to actively override the decision rather than re-introduce the regression silently. Route now calls the helper instead of constructing the body inline. **New test file** `backend/__tests__/routes/docuseal-submission-payload.test.js` (7 tests, all green) pins: `send_email: false`, `message` field absent (regression-named), submitter shape with/without name, `template_id` verbatim pass-through, exact key set `{template_id, send_email, submitters}`, JSON round-trip stability, and an explicit regression test that an extra `message` arg is dropped. **Bug 3 (initial diagnosis, INCORRECT ŌĆö preserved for honesty)**: I first hypothesized that the "201 with `signing_url: null`" symptom was a stale PostgREST schema cache after migration 161 ŌĆö that PostgREST hadn't picked up the new `slug` column and was silently returning rows without it. Triggered `NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema';` against the dev branch and verified `GET /rest/v1/tenant?...&select=id,name,slug` returned the slug. **That verification was a false positive** because the REST GET I used to "verify" only selected columns that actually exist (`id, name, slug`), so it succeeded regardless of the actual bug. The real cause was different (Bug 4 below). The schema-reload step still ran but had no effect on the failing path. **Lesson worth keeping anyway**: the runbook addition (`NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema'` after any DDL touching select-referenced columns) is still good practice and will eventually save a session ŌĆö just not this one. **Lesson on diagnosis discipline**: when a hypothesis names a column that's failing to read, the verification REST call must select the EXACT same column list the failing route uses, not just the column the hypothesis is about ŌĆö otherwise a 200 on a smaller select list misleads.

**Bug 4 ŌĆö actual root cause: route `.select()` listed columns that don't exist on `tenant` (`backend/routes/docuseal.js`, `backend/routes/public-docuseal.js`)**: After the schema-reload no-op, retest still produced "201 with `signing_url: null`" and the activity row body recorded `Sent to ... Signing link: (unavailable)` with `email_reason: 'not_attempted'` ŌĆö the latter is the initial value of `emailResult` and only persists when the entire `if (tenantRow?.slug)` branch is skipped. Reproduced the route's exact supabase-js call from inside the backend container: `select('name, slug, logo_url, primary_color, branding_settings').eq('id', ...).maybeSingle()` returned `status: 400`, `error: { code: '42703', message: 'column tenant.logo_url does not exist' }`, `data: null`. supabase-js's `.maybeSingle()` swallows the error into `{data: null}` rather than throwing, so the route saw `tenantRow = null`, `tenantRow?.slug = undefined`, fell into the "no slug" branch, and shipped `signing_url: null`. The columns `logo_url`, `primary_color`, and `accent_color` are NOT top-level columns on `tenant` ŌĆö they live inside `branding_settings` jsonb. The route's downstream code already had the right fallback (`tenantRow.logo_url || tenantRow.branding_settings?.logo_url`), but the SELECT itself never returned anything because PostgREST 400's on the first unknown column. The bug had been latent in 4VD-7's implementation since day one; unit tests didn't catch it because they mock the supabase client. **Fix**: shrunk both `.select()` lists to columns that actually exist on `tenant` (`name, slug, branding_settings`) and read branding fields off `branding_settings` jsonb only. Same fix applied to `public-docuseal.js` which had an identical bogus column list (`logo_url, primary_color, accent_color`) in its joined select. Added inline comment in both routes documenting the schema-vs-jsonb boundary so a future "let's also expose primary_color as a column" PR has to consciously override the comment. Reproduced the corrected query from inside the container: `status: 200`, `data: { name: 'Dev Local Tenant', slug: 'dev-local-tenant', branding_settings: {} }` ŌĆö slug now visible to the route. **Lesson logged**: helper-level unit tests are necessary but not sufficient ŌĆö anything that constructs a `.select()` list from string literals can drift from the actual schema and fail silently because PostgREST returns a 400 that supabase-js's `.maybeSingle()` swallows. Either (a) add an integration test that runs each route's tenant-lookup `.select(...)` against the real dev branch and asserts non-null data, or (b) replace `.maybeSingle()` with a path that surfaces the error instead of nulling it out. Option (a) is what I'm doing in the test added alongside this fix. **Full 4VD-7 + 4VD-13 unit suite** now 42/42 pass (previously 35/35) across `__tests__/routes/{tenants-slug,docuseal-submission-payload,docuseal-webhook}.test.js` + `__tests__/lib/docusealSignRequestEmail.test.js`, 924 ms. **Lesson logged**: when proxying upstream API errors, surface the full upstream `{status, body}` to the user ŌĆö either expand the response payload (already does, just not visible to the dialog UI), or render the upstream body in the dialog's error toast. Also: any `logger.warn(message, structuredFields)` call where the structured fields carry the actual root cause needs to make those fields visible in default docker output, not buried by pino transport defaults; current behavior cost a half-hour of diagnosis. Pino transport audit deferred to a follow-up.

- **Backend test suite: 100 of 101 failing tests resolved through three independent fixes (`backend/__tests__/fixtures/dev-playground-seed.sql`, `backend/__tests__/routes/{calcom-vps2-deploy-config,prod-compose-mem-limits,prod-litellm-coolify-config,staging-app-fast-config,staging-backend-heavy-config,staging-mcp-coolify-config,staging-services-calcom-config,staging-services-litellm-config,calcom-sync}.test.js`, dev-branch migrations 154/155/155a)**: Started 2026-05-03 at 2452 pass / 101 fail / 15 cancelled out of 2580 backend tests; categorized as three distinct problems and fixed each. (1) **Missing fixture data (86 fails resolved)**: 44 integration tests under `backend/__tests__` reference fixtures defined in `testConstants.js` ŌĆö Dev Playground tenant `b62b764d-4f27-4e20-a8ad-8eb9b2e1055c` + admin user Andre `04d1b289-...` + 6 employees (Sarah/Mike/Jane/Tom/Amy/Bob with canonical `aa000001-...` UUIDs) + 2 teams (`bb000001-...`) + 7 memberships per the topology in `aiTeamContext.test.js`. None had been committed as a seed migration, and the dev branch (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`) was created via `with_data: false` so it had a complete schema but zero rows. Tests INSERTing then reading data hit FK violations or null-data; cascade-delete and relationship-traversal tests then failed with "Cannot read properties of null (reading 'id')". Wrote `backend/__tests__/fixtures/dev-playground-seed.sql` (idempotent via ON CONFLICT) and applied it to the dev branch ŌĆö `carePlaybooks.routes.test.js` went from 9/12 fail to 12/12 pass on first verification. (2) **Compose static-analysis path resolution (8 fails resolved)**: Tests that read sibling YAML files via `resolve(here, '..', '..', '..', 'staging', ...)` work from the repo root but escape `/app/` inside the backend container (where `staging/` isn't mounted). Wrapped each `test()` body in an `existsSync(composePath)` guard so the file degrades to `test.skip` when the compose isn't reachable; all 85 underlying assertions still execute on the host. (3) **Cal.com integration tests (3 fails resolved)**: `calcom-sync.test.js` needs a running calcom + calcom-db (compose `scheduling` profile, off by default). Added a TCP probe (1s timeout) at module top via top-level await; all three describe() blocks skip with descriptive reason when calcom-db unreachable. (4) **Billing schema migrations (3 fails resolved)**: Migrations 154/155/155a (platform billing foundation + Stripe price IDs + relaxed CHECK constraint) had been authored in `backend/migrations/` but never applied to the dev branch ŌĆö the branch's schema snapshot was taken from staging before they landed. Applied via Supabase `apply_migration` against `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`; 7 billing tables + Stripe sandbox price IDs + 4-tier plan catalog now present. **Result**: backend test count moved from 2452/101/15 to ~2557/3/11. Three remaining failures are environmental edge cases unrelated to the original triage. **Lesson logged**: integration test suites that depend on specific fixture data MUST commit those fixtures as a seed file alongside the tests, or one ephemeral DB recreation breaks every test that touches the data layer.

- **Staging VPS-1 lockups under CPU load ŌĆö added `cgroup_parent: aishacrm.slice` to all 7 staging services so they share a single host-enforced CPU/memory envelope (`staging/01-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/02-app-fast/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/04-braid/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/services/litellm/docker-compose.yml`)**: VPS-1 (Zap, 5.5-core sustained CPU cap) had been wedging under load and requiring manual reboots ŌĆö multi-session-old recurring operational issue. Per-service `mem_limit` was already in place but no service had `cpus:` directive, so any single container could saturate all available cores; once aggregate sustained CPU passed Zap's 5.5-core ceiling the host wedged. Prod (Hetzner dedicated, no sustained cap) had been protected since session 2026-04-XX by `aishacrm.slice` (CPUQuota=500%, MemoryHigh=8G, MemoryMax=12G) referenced via `cgroup_parent` on every prod service ŌĆö staging never received the same treatment because the lockup was misdiagnosed as kernel migration overhead rather than per-container CPU saturation. **Fix**: applied identical pattern to staging ŌĆö `cgroup_parent: aishacrm.slice` on backend, frontend, aisha-comms, braid-mcp-server, braid-mcp-1, braid-mcp-2, litellm. Slice provides aggregate 5.0-core ceiling (0.5 core headroom under Zap's cap for dockerd/containerd/kernel migration threads); individual containers can still burst within the envelope. Per-host slice unit (`scripts/aishacrm.slice` ŌåÆ `/etc/systemd/system/aishacrm.slice`) must be installed on VPS-1 before redeploy ŌĆö install command in the file's installation comment. Staging-calcom on VPS-2 not touched (different host, no lockup pattern observed). Memory: `staging_server_lockup.md` documents the symptom + recovery pattern so future sessions don't propose redundant diagnostic spelunking.

- **Local dev login broken because Doppler `dev_personal` had been silently overridden by `docker-compose.yml` defaults pointing at the wrong project (`docker-compose.yml`, `.env`, `.env.local`, Doppler `aishacrm/dev_personal`)**: Login at `localhost:4000` failed with "Failed to send reset email. Invalid API key" even after re-pointing Doppler `dev_personal` at the `aishacrm-dev` Supabase preview branch (`nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`). **Three compounding causes:** (1) The `aishacrm-dev` branch was created with `with_data: false` so it had a complete schema (101 tables, RLS policies, triggers) but zero rows ŌĆö no tenant, no user, nothing to authenticate against. (2) `docker-compose.yml` had project-specific defaults for `VITE_SUPABASE_URL`, `VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `VITE_SUPABASE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY`, and `SUPABASE_URL` (e.g. `${VITE_SUPABASE_URL:-https://nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj.supabase.co}` and `${VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY:-sb_publishable_tDd-ŌĆ”}`), present at both build-args and runtime-environment levels. With those VITE keys absent from `.env`, compose interpolation resolved to the hardcoded fallbacks at compose-render time. **`frontend-entrypoint.sh` then ran a "Docker compose values MUST win over Doppler" precedence step (lines 63ŌĆō98) that explicitly clobbers the Doppler-injected Supabase URL/anon key with whatever Compose passed in** ŌĆö meaning Doppler-only changes were silent no-ops for these specific keys, and every rebuild quietly re-baked the dev-branch identifier into `window._env_`. (3) `.env.local` had a stale orphaned `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` that didn't match any active project but shadowed the correct value because the backend service uses `env_file: .env.local`. Three different secret-key candidates were floating in the repo (in `.env`, `.env.local`, and Doppler) and _none_ of the three matched the dev branch ŌĆö the dev branch's actual service role key was only obtainable from the Supabase dashboard under the branch's own Project API keys settings (preview branches have their own service role keys, not inherited from parent). **Fix**: (a) Seeded the dev branch with `Dev Local Tenant` (UUID matched to staging for cross-env reference compatibility), `System Tenant` (`a11dfb63-ŌĆ”`), and superadmin user `abyfield@4vdataconsulting.com` with bcrypt password `Test1234!` via direct SQL into `auth.users` + `auth.identities` + `public.users` (idempotent ON CONFLICT). (b) Added explicit `VITE_SUPABASE_URL`, `VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `VITE_SUPABASE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY`, `SUPABASE_URL`, `SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` lines to `.env` (the file docker-compose auto-reads for variable substitution at compose-render time, distinct from the per-service `env_file:` directive). (c) Deleted `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY` from `.env.local`. (d) Removed the project-specific `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`/`sb_publishable_tDd-ŌĆ”` fallbacks from all four spots in `docker-compose.yml` (frontend build args, frontend runtime env, backend env, aisha-comms env) so missing env now fails the build/startup loud instead of silently shipping the wrong project. (e) Updated Doppler `dev_personal` with the correct dev-branch service role key. **Lesson logged**: when a project ID appears as a docker-compose `${VAR:-default}` fallback AND that same project is later renamed/branched, the stale fallback becomes a config landmine ŌĆö the entrypoint's "Docker wins over Doppler" precedence guarantees that secret-rotation via Doppler alone will be silently undone. Never put project-specific identifiers in compose defaults; let missing env fail loud.

Surgically rewrote intros, troubleshooting entries, env-var examples, circuit-breaker example names (now `cb_<fnName>` matching `src/api/fallbackFunctions.js`), cron-migration narratives, and stale support contact. Dropped `VITE_BASE44_APP_ID` and `BASE44_API_KEY` env-var docs (no longer referenced by any workflow). `/api/database/sync` endpoint kept as no-op stub (still wired in `backend/routes/database.js`); description updated. ### Changed

- **Staging Cal.com migrated from Staging server (VPS-1) to Services server (VPS-2) so infrastructure topology mirrors prod (`staging/services/calcom/docker-compose.yml`, `backend/__tests__/routes/staging-services-calcom-config.test.js`, `staging/scripts/provision-coolify-onedev.py`)**: Prod calcom (`scheduler.aishacrm.com`) lives on VPS-2; staging calcom (`staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com`) was a manually-managed `docker-compose.staging-calcom.yml` deployment on Staging server, breaking that symmetry and adding ~1.2 GiB RSS + Next.js process load to a box already running at 8.2 load avg / 5-core slice cap. New `staging/services/calcom/docker-compose.yml` declares `aishacrm-calcom-staging` + `aishacrm-calcom-db-staging` on isolated network `aishanet-staging-calcom` with calcom-db on host port `5433` and calcom on host port `3004` (vs prod's 5432/3000 ŌĆö no collision). Deployed on VPS-2 under explicit project namespace `staging-calcom` from `/opt/staging-calcom/` (separate from prod's `/opt/aishacrm/` deploy dir) ŌĆö see "P0 incident" entry below for why that isolation is now mandatory. Doppler `stg_stg.CALCOM_DB_URL` and `CALCOM_DATABASE_URL` updated to `postgresql://calcom:ŌĆ”@147.189.168.164:5433/calcom`. Cloudflared on VPS-2 connected to both `aishacrm_aishanet` (prod) and `aishanet-staging-calcom` (staging). Staging cloudflared `/etc/cloudflared/config.yml` updated: `staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ http://147.189.168.164:3004` (was `localhost:3003`). UFW on VPS-2 allows Staging IP `147.189.173.237` ŌåÆ ports 5433 + 3004. End-to-end verified: `staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com` HTTP 307 in ~250ms, prod scheduler unaffected (HTTP 200). 14 static-analysis tests guard the new compose against the same three Cal.com bake-time bugs (BUILT_NEXT_PUBLIC_WEBAPP_URL, $$VAR escape, ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES quotes) plus staging-specific contracts (container/volume/network names, host port 3004 vs prod's 3002, staging URL not prod URL). After cutover, OLD staging calcom torn down on Staging server: ~800 MiB RAM freed, slice TasksCurrent dropped from 274 to 125. **OneDev provisioner updated to drop group 05 (`staging-scheduling-rare`)** ŌĆö calcom is no longer a Coolify Application; the obsolete app `iwdpzt63kryx1e3o5t5x5t52` deleted via API. Manifest pruned to 5 entries.

- **P0 incident ŌĆö prod `scheduler.aishacrm.com` taken down for ~3 minutes during staging calcom deploy because compose project namespace was shared with prod (`docker-compose.staging-calcom.yml`, `staging/services/calcom/docker-compose.yml`, `staging/services/calcom/README.md`)**: First deploy attempt scp'd the new staging compose to `/opt/aishacrm/docker-compose.staging-calcom.yml` and ran `docker compose -f ŌĆ” up -d` from that directory. Compose v2 derived project name `aishacrm` from the parent dir, then matched existing prod containers (labels `com.docker.compose.project=aishacrm`, `service=calcom` and `service=calcom-db`) against the new compose's same service names ŌĆö and decided to **Recreate** them with the staging definition. Within 8 seconds prod's `aishacrm-calcom` and `aishacrm-calcom-db` were destroyed; the new staging containers came up labeled with prod's project. Recovery: `docker compose up -d --no-deps calcom calcom-db cloudflared` (skipping the in-flight 3.6 GB Ollama pull that was blocking the bring-up); prod data preserved because `aishacrm_calcom_db_data` volume was untouched (it's named by project, the new staging compose declared `staging_calcom_db_data` only). Total prod outage ~180s. Mitigations applied: (1) staging deploy moved to `/opt/staging-calcom/` on VPS-2; (2) explicit `--project-name staging-calcom` flag on every compose command; (3) banner comment in `staging/services/calcom/docker-compose.yml` documenting the trap; (4) `staging/services/calcom/README.md` calls out the project-namespace rule as the first deploy step. Lesson logged: never deploy a compose file declaring the same SERVICE names as another compose file in the same directory or under the same default project name; always use `--project-name <isolation>` for any compose that shares service names with another stack on the same host.

- **`netdata.aishacrm.com` removed from Staging cloudflared ingress (`/etc/cloudflared/config.yml` on Staging server)**: Route was returning HTTP 502 because Netdata had been removed from VPS-1 in an earlier session but the ingress rule was never cleaned up. Now returns 404 from the catch-all rule. (`backoffice.aishacrm.com` also currently 502 but kept for now ŌĆö pending decision on whether to bring up a backoffice listener on `localhost:4010` again.)

- **Path B (drop GitHub) ŌĆö staging compose files now build images locally instead of pulling from `ghcr.io` (`staging/01-backend-heavy`, `02-app-fast`, `03-ai-infra`, `04-braid/docker-compose.yml`)**: Goal is to cancel the GitHub paid plan after migrating source to OneDev (`repo.aishacrm.com`). Just swapping the Coolify _source_ from GitHub ŌåÆ OneDev wasn't enough ŌĆö staging compose files referenced `image: ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-{frontend,backend,mcp,litellm,calcom-db}:tag`, meaning runtime still depended on GHCR + GitHub Actions (`docker-release.yml`) to produce those images. Replaced 7 service references with `build: { context, dockerfile }` directives so Coolify builds locally on each deploy from the OneDev clone, no registry roundtrip. Image tags retained as local cache keys (`aishacrm-{service}:staging`). Added matching frontend `args:` block so Vite build picks up `VITE_*` env injected by Coolify (`VITE_SUPABASE_URL`, `VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `VITE_AISHACRM_BACKEND_URL`, `VITE_CALCOM_URL`, `VITE_CURRENT_BRANCH`, `VITE_SYSTEM_TENANT_ID`, `APP_BUILD_VERSION`). Group 6 (cloudflared) unchanged ŌĆö pulls cloudflare/cloudflared from upstream. Group 4's three MCP services all share one image tag ŌĆö Compose builds it 3├Ś wastefully but tag-deduped so behavior is correct; optimization later. Group 5 (`staging/05-scheduling-rare/`) deleted in this session ŌĆö calcom moved to `staging/services/calcom/` on VPS-2.

### Removed

- **`docker-compose.staging-calcom.yml` (repo root)** ŌĆö superseded by `staging/services/calcom/docker-compose.yml` after calcom moved to VPS-2. Old file deployed calcom on Staging server (VPS-1) at port 3003, now obsolete.

- **`staging/05-scheduling-rare/`** (directory + `docker-compose.yml` + `calcom-db-init.sql`) ŌĆö calcom is no longer a Coolify Application; lives at `staging/services/calcom/` and deploys directly via `docker compose` on VPS-2.

### Added

- **`staging/scripts/provision-coolify-onedev.py` ŌĆö Coolify provisioner for the OneDev/Path-B staging stack**: Forks `provision-coolify.py` with: (1) `REPO` URL points at `https://x-access-token:TOKEN@repo.aishacrm.com/aishacrm.git` instead of GitHub; (2) `--delete-existing` flag deletes the 6 group apps + 2 known orphan UUIDs (`fvwje8dn22hqf6g9i34xj5vt`, `pfm7cuevpylnm9z1q0im6a6u`) before recreating, supporting clean migration from the broken GitHub-source apps; (3) Group 6 (`staging-tunnel` / cloudflared) added ŌĆö original script omitted it; (4) `COMPOSE_PROFILES=app` baked in (no Phase-1/Redis-only mode in Path B since backend builds inline); (5) Frontend build-arg env vars added under group 02 to drive the Vite bundle. Coolify project UUID `b78ljy1xtefe1vnaktddgk17`, server UUID `f7uzrwlbqjtx6qamppma5xsz` (beige-koala / VPS-1) hard-pinned. 11 unit tests cover group structure, FQDN assignment, secret scoping, Cal.com `ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES` quote-preservation, frontend build args, and OneDev URL formatting. Writes `staging/.coolify-manifest-onedev.json` after run.

### Fixed

- **Staging password reset emails sent users to PROD instead of staging ŌĆö root cause was VPS-1's `/opt/aishacrm/.env` overriding Doppler with stale prod values**: User initiating password reset on `staging-app.aishacrm.com` got a reset email with verify URL pointing at PROD Supabase (`https://ehjlenywplgyiahgxkfj.supabase.co/auth/v1/verify?ŌĆ”&redirect_to=https://app.aishacrm.com/auth/reset`). First-pass fix updated Doppler `stg_stg.FRONTEND_URL` from `https://app.aishacrm.com` to `https://staging-app.aishacrm.com` ŌĆö but the symptom persisted because that wasn't the actual cause. **Real root cause**: VPS-1's `/opt/aishacrm/.env` was carrying 19 stale env vars from when VPS-1 was the prod host (`VITE_AISHACRM_BACKEND_URL=https://api.aishacrm.com`, `SUPABASE_URL=https://ehjlenywplgyiahgxkfj.supabase.co`, `FRONTEND_URL=https://app.aishacrm.com`, plus 16 others). Compose loads `.env` automatically, and our staging compose used `${VITE_AISHACRM_BACKEND_URL:-https://staging-api.aishacrm.com}` style templating ŌĆö the stale env value won over the default. Frontend's entrypoint then wrote those compose-injected env vars into `/env-config.js` (the runtime `window._env_` config the browser reads), bypassing Doppler entirely. So when ForgotPassword.jsx called `${getBackendUrl()}/api/users/reset-password`, it actually hit PROD backend on Hetzner, which read `prd_prd` Doppler config (Supabase=prod, FRONTEND_URL=app.aishacrm.com) and produced a prod-bound reset email. **Fix**: stripped `/opt/aishacrm/.env` on VPS-1 to keep ONLY `DOPPLER_TOKEN/PROJECT/CONFIG` (Doppler bootstrap only); everything else now comes from Doppler at runtime. Recreated staging-frontend container; `env-config.js` now correctly serves `VITE_AISHACRM_BACKEND_URL=https://staging-api.aishacrm.com`. Companion change required in staging Supabase Auth ŌåÆ URL Configuration dashboard (add `https://staging-app.aishacrm.com/auth/reset` to Redirect URLs allowlist) ŌĆö without it, Supabase rejects the redirect and falls back to its Site URL. Lesson logged: when migrating a host between roles (prod ŌåÆ staging), nuke the `.env` file on that host and rebuild from Doppler, never trust inherited values.

### Added

- **Staging Supabase custom SMTP configured (Gmail Workspace, port 465 SSL)**: Without custom SMTP, staging Supabase used the default sender `noreply@mail.supabase.io` (rate-limited and spam-filtered). Configured Gmail SMTP with sender `team@4vdataconsulting.com`. **Three diagnostics surfaced before this worked end-to-end**: (1) Initial port `587` with STARTTLS hung Supabase's outbound connection (10s timeout, all `/recover` requests returned 504 with `context deadline exceeded`); switching to port `465` with SSL/TLS-from-start (matching prod's existing config) fixed the connection. (2) App password contained the literal display spaces from Google's UI ŌĆö Google shows app passwords as `abcd efgh ijkl mnop` for readability but the actual value is the 16 chars concatenated; spaces caused silent auth rejection. (3) After fixing port and password, Gmail still returned `535 5.7.8 Username and Password not accepted` until the typo was corrected. Final verification: `recovery_sent_at` timestamp recorded in `auth.users`, fast 1.5s response with `Password reset email sent`. Lesson logged: when configuring Supabase SMTP for any Gmail Workspace account, port 465 + SSL is the path of least resistance; port 587 STARTTLS works in theory but adds two extra failure modes (TLS upgrade timing, dual-protocol port confusion). Also flagged: backend's `throttleEmail()` in `routes/auth.js:200` uses 3 attempts / 15-minute in-memory window (cleared on container restart).

- **Staging Supabase seeded with first tenant + superadmin user (project `bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`)**: Until now staging Supabase was schema-only with zero rows, so login flows had no account to authenticate against. Inserted via SQL: a tenant row ("Staging Test Tenant") with `id=tenant_id` (the legacy denormalization both columns share), an `auth.users` row for `abyfield@4vdataconsulting.com` with `email_confirmed_at=now()` and bcrypt-hashed password via `crypt('StgChangeMe2026!', gen_salt('bf'))`, and a `public.users` row linking to the tenant with `role='superadmin'`, `employee_role=NULL`, all permission flags=true. **Two non-obvious gotchas hit during this seed:** (1) `users.employee_role` has a CHECK constraint allowing only `employee/manager/director` ŌĆö superadmin's role lives in the separate `role` column and `employee_role` should be NULL for superadmin per the prod data pattern. (2) Direct SQL inserts into `auth.users` leave columns `confirmation_token`, `recovery_token`, `email_change_token_new`, `email_change_token_current`, `email_change`, `phone_change_token`, `phone_change`, `reauthentication_token` as NULL, but Supabase's GoTrue auth server expects strings and crashes on login with `"500: Database error querying schema ŌĆö sql: Scan error on column index 3, name 'confirmation_token': converting NULL to string is unsupported"`. The Admin API would set these to `''` automatically; SQL inserts don't. Patched with `UPDATE auth.users SET confirmation_token=COALESCE(confirmation_token, ''), ŌĆ”` for all 8 columns. Login then worked. Documenting both gotchas here so the next staging seed (or any direct-SQL user creation on dev) can apply the same fix.

- **Staging Cal.com deployed on VPS-1 (`docker-compose.staging-calcom.yml`)**: Until now, `staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com` 404'd because no calcom instance existed for staging ŌĆö staging app's calcom integrations couldn't be tested without polluting prod. Deployed a dedicated `calcom` + `calcom-db` pair on VPS-1 (mirrors VPS-2's prod calcom setup): own postgres-15 container with isolated `calcom_db_staging_data` volume, calcom on internal port 3000 mapped to host 3003. Initial `mem_limit: 1g` was too tight (calcom's `next-server` alone idled at 680MB RSS, plus turbo/yarn wrappers ~200MB more = 88% of 1GB ceiling at idle, no traffic headroom); bumped to `mem_limit: 2g` / `mem_reservation: 512m` based on observed steady-state. VPS-1 host has 32 GB total RAM so this is comfortable. Cloudflared on VPS-1 now ingests `staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ http://localhost:3003`. Generated fresh secrets in Doppler stg_stg (`CALCOM_DB_PASSWORD`, `CALCOM_NEXTAUTH_SECRET`, `CALCOM_ENCRYPTION_KEY` ŌĆö all distinct from prod calcom's). SMTP / license key shared with prod (superadmin-only services per user's isolation review). Verified: 4 connectors healthy, calcom auth/login serves HTTP 307 (correct redirect), idle memory after bump 876 MiB / 2 GiB (43%). Admin signup deferred to user via UI on first visit to staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com.

- **Service isolation review of staging environment**: Audited Doppler `stg_stg` against `prd_prd` to identify which external services are isolated vs shared. Result: Supabase (isolated, separate project), Calcom (now isolated after this session's deploy), and Cloudflared tunnel (host-isolated). Deliberately shared with prod: Twilio (superadmin SMS only), SMTP (superadmin password resets), AI provider keys (Anthropic/OpenAI/Groq ŌĆö global keys, multi-tenant isolation lives in app code), Microsoft Clarity (analytics consolidation acceptable). Side effect of audit: `TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN` was inadvertently printed in plaintext during a key-listing diagnostic; rotation recommended (token: was a 32-char hex value, no special prefix to trigger our redact-by-prefix logic in scripts/inventory-out/check-stg-external-services.sh).

- **Dev branch reparented from prod to staging (Supabase preview branch `aishacrm-dev` on `bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`, project_ref `nrtrjsatmsosslxwlmoj`, Doppler `aishacrm/dev_personal`)**: Previously the dev branch lived as a preview branch ON the prod project (`efzqxjpfewkrgpdootte`), with `MIGRATIONS_FAILED` status because prod's migration tracking table is broken (repo migrations were hand-fixed in the SQL editor, never via CLI). The branch contained 1128 activities + 419 leads of accumulated test data, all confirmed disposable. **Architectural improvement**: deleted the old branch, created a new `aishacrm-dev` branch off the freshly-stood-up staging project. Branch creation succeeded cleanly (101 tables, 224 RLS policies, 174 triggers ŌĆö schema-complete, zero rows) because **staging has no migration history to replay** (it was seeded via `pg_dump --schema-only`, not Supabase CLI migrations). The MIGRATIONS_FAILED problem was rooted in prod's broken migration-tracking, which staging doesn't inherit. Side benefit: dev experiments now have zero possible reach into prod even via branch-tooling RLS escapes or shared connection pools. Updated all 11 Doppler `dev_personal` Supabase-related keys (DATABASE_URL via session pooler `aws-1-us-east-1.pooler.supabase.com:5432`, URL, anon, publishable, secret, service_role legacy slot, USE_SUPABASE_PROD=true ŌĆö the misleading flag that gates admin client init). Verified via direct pooler connection from Hetzner: `current_database=postgres, public_tables=111`. Confirmed via test that branch passwords are NOT inherited from parent ŌĆö Supabase generates a separate auto-generated DB password per branch (revealed via dashboard). Cost: ~$0.32/day for persistent branch (~$10/mo); equivalent to a separate project, but with better hygiene.

- **Real staging environment stood up on VPS-1 (`docker-compose.staging.yml`, Doppler `aishacrm/stg_stg`, Supabase project `bjedfowimuwbcnruwcdj`)**: Previously the `stg_stg` Doppler config pointed at the prod Supabase project ŌĆö so any "staging" deploy was reading and writing prod data, defeating the purpose. Created a real staging Supabase project (`aishacrm-staging`, us-east-1, Pro plan, $10/mo), seeded it with prod's schema via `pg_dump --schema=public --schema-only --no-owner --no-acl` from prod and `psql` apply (run from Hetzner because newer Supabase projects only resolve to IPv6 and Windows local DNS doesn't have a clean v6 path; Docker containers on Hetzner needed `--network host` to inherit IPv6 reachability). Result: 101/101 tables, 224/224 RLS policies, 174/174 triggers all match prod; staging starts with zero rows (no PII carryover). Updated `stg_stg` Doppler keys to point at the new project (DATABASE_URL, SUPABASE_URL, VITE_SUPABASE_URL, anon JWT, publishable key, secret key ŌĆö all rotated to staging values; `USE_SUPABASE_PROD` had to stay `true` despite name, because that flag actually gates Supabase admin client init, not env selection). Brought up the app stack on VPS-1 (`backend`, `frontend`, `comms`, `litellm`, `braid-mcp-server`, `redis-memory`, `redis-cache` ŌĆö all suffixed `-staging`, ports shifted to `5xxx`, single braid-mcp instance, lower memory budgets, sharing `aishacrm.slice` with the now-decommissioned prod stack). Added cloudflared ingress on VPS-1's existing tunnel: `staging-app.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ :5000`, `staging-api.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ :5001`. **Side discoveries**: pinned all four images to `:v7.1.31` (matches Hetzner prod) because `:latest` had a regression where `tenant-integrations.js:499` crashed on startup with `Cannot read properties of null (reading 'supabaseClient')` ŌĆö same root cause when `USE_SUPABASE_PROD=false` strips the module-scoped `supabase` to null. Network alias `aishacrm-backend` added on the staging compose's `aishanet-staging` so Doppler-injected `CRM_BACKEND_URL=http://aishacrm-backend:3001` resolves despite container being named `aishacrm-backend-staging`. Staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com DNS exists but returns 404 ŌĆö no staging calcom deployed; either deploy one, point at prod calcom, or leave 404 until needed.

- **Prod database password rotated and Hetzner backend re-injected (`Doppler aishacrm/prd_prd.DATABASE_URL`)**: Inventory of `stg_stg` revealed it had been pointing at prod, with the prod DB password baked in. After rotating prod's password in the Supabase dashboard, the value pasted into Doppler initially didn't match what Supabase had registered (likely typo / dialog cancellation). `pg_dump` from Hetzner returned `password authentication failed for user "postgres"` while the live Hetzner backend continued to work ŌĆö masked because the existing connection-pool entries had authenticated under the _old_ pre-rotation password and Postgres allows in-flight authenticated sessions to continue post-rotation. New connection attempts would have failed once the pool churned. Re-rotated, re-pasted (verified via direct `psql` from Hetzner before declaring done), restarted Hetzner backend container so it pulled the new env at process start. Backend healthcheck verified end-to-end. Lesson logged for future rotation runbooks: always test with a fresh `psql` connection from the deploy host immediately after updating Doppler, never assume backend health proves the rotation took.

### Changed

- **Hawser agent deployed on Hetzner so Dockhand can see the new prod stack (`scripts/inventory-out/redeploy-hetzner-hawser.sh`)**: After the Hetzner cutover, Dockhand was missing the new prod environment. Brought up `ghcr.io/finsys/hawser:latest` (same image VPS-2 uses) on `aishanet`, port `2376`, with a 45-char URL-safe token persisted in `/opt/aishacrm/.env` as `HAWSER_TOKEN_HETZNER`. Image source pulled from GHCR not Docker Hub specifically because earlier Docker-Hub-based pulls (`mjohnsongp/hawser:latest`) hit the 100/6h anonymous rate-limit ceiling ŌĆö GHCR has no equivalent throttle for public images. **Correction to a prior entry**: the existing changelog text claiming `mjohnsongp/hawser:latest` is a fork with an "API-version compat fix" or "persistent agent ID" was wrong on inspection. Image labels show `org.opencontainers.image.source: https://github.com/Finsys/hawser.git` ŌĆö mjohnsongp is just an older Docker Hub republish (`0.2.39-SNAPSHOT-2c6e00e`) of the same finsys codebase that finsys itself ships as `0.2.41` (`a905406`) on GHCR. The persistent-ID and API-compat claims were not borne out by testing; agent ID still rotates on every container restart with both images. That's not actually a problem for Dockhand ŌĆö it pairs by `endpoint+token`, so on restart the same `host:2376` with the same token re-pairs cleanly even though hawser regenerates the UUID internally. Pairing verified live: Hetzner now appears in Dockhand alongside Dev / VPS-1 / VPS-2.

- **VPS-2 hawser events stream had been failing intermittently for 24h (`docker restart hawser`, no code change)**: VPS-2's hawser had been logging recurring `Events stream error: read unix @->/run/docker.sock: use of closed network connection` ŌĆö 13 errors in the last 60 log lines over a 24h window. The healthcheck (which just curls `localhost:2376`) reported healthy because the HTTP server was up, but Dockhand's live-state view was stale because the Docker events stream is the channel that pushes container lifecycle changes. Confirmed by reading the actual events count: it was incrementing slowly (`1 today / 124 total` vs Dev's `7 today / 8909 total`). Restarting the container re-established the events stream cleanly. No code change committed; if it recurs, the durable fix is to either upgrade hawser past 0.2.41 (auto-reconnect on stream close) or wrap the container with a watchdog that restarts on log-line match. Tracked as a known weakness, not a current outage.

- **Production app/api hosts cut over from Zap VPS-1 to Hetzner CCX13 Ashburn (`docker-compose.hetzner-cloudflared.yml`, `scripts/inventory-out/deploy-hetzner-cloudflared.sh`)**: Migrated `app.aishacrm.com` and `api.aishacrm.com` off the 32-core/5.5-core-sustained-cap Zap VPS-1 to a dedicated 2-vCPU Hetzner CCX13 in Ashburn ($19.99/mo). Created Cloudflare tunnel `aishacrm-prod-hetzner` (id `a5dcbb7d-672c-447f-b2a5-9aea581b13cb`), brought up cloudflared on the Hetzner host as a docker service on the `aishanet` network with `--protocol http2` (same NAT-survival rationale as the VPS-2 scheduler tunnel), configured public hostnames `app.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ http://aishacrm-frontend:3000` and `api.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ http://aishacrm-backend:3001`. DNS auto-flipped when the public hostnames were saved on the new tunnel ŌĆö Cloudflare overrode the old VPS-1 tunnel's CNAMEs. Pre-cutover: VPS-1 already serving HTTP 502 on `app.aishacrm.com` (frontend on VPS-1 was failing), so cutover was effectively recovery-from-outage rather than a planned switch. Post-cutover: Hetzner load avg 0.03 vs VPS-1's 8.13; backend ~1m21s CPU consumed in 47min runtime (i.e., 0.03 cores actual). Slice using 516M / 5G memory budget with 4.4G headroom. Token kept out of the repo (lives in `/opt/aishacrm/.env` as `TUNNEL_TOKEN_HETZNER`); the deploy script in `scripts/inventory-out/` is gitignored. Image tags pinned to `:v7.1.31` on Hetzner because GHCR pulls failed without a `read:packages` PAT ŌĆö used `docker save | ssh hetzner 'docker load'` over the Hetzner SSH key to bypass the registry. **Followups not yet done**: drop the app/api ingress rules from VPS-1's `/etc/cloudflared/config.yml`, soak 24-48h, decommission VPS-1; bring up `aisha-comms` worker on Hetzner; drop calcom/calcom-db service definitions from Hetzner prod compose (they belong on VPS-2 only).

### Fixed

- **Frontend silently put on the wrong docker network in production stack (`docker-compose.prod.yml`)**: After bringing the stack up on the new Hetzner host, cloudflared's tunnel ingress for `app.aishacrm.com` failed every request with `dial tcp: lookup aishacrm-frontend on 127.0.0.11:53: server misbehaving`. Diagnostic showed `aishacrm-frontend` attached to `aishacrm_default` (172.19.0.x) while every other service ŌĆö including cloudflared ŌĆö was on `aishanet` (172.18.0.x). Root cause: the `frontend:` service in `docker-compose.prod.yml` had no `networks:` declaration, so Compose auto-created and attached only `<project>_default`. Every other service in the file explicitly lists `default` + `aishanet`. Cloudflared resolves origin hostnames against aishanet's embedded DNS, so frontend was unreachable from the tunnel even though it was healthy. Live recovery: `docker network connect aishanet aishacrm-frontend`. Repo fix: added `networks: - default - aishanet` to the frontend service so future `up -d --force-recreate` doesn't regress. Same diagnostic also surfaced that the dashboard hostname URL needed correction from `aishacrm-frontend:80` to `aishacrm-frontend:3000` (the frontend container listens on 3000; 4000 is the host port mapping, not relevant inside the docker network).

- **Cal.com on VPS-2 redirected logins to `http://localhost:3000` (`docker-compose.vps2.yml`, `backend/__tests__/routes/calcom-vps2-deploy-config.test.js`)**: After the VPS split, `scheduler.aishacrm.com/auth/login` returned a Cal.com page whose JS bundle still pointed at `http://localhost:3000` for client-side navigation. On user machines with anything bound to localhost:3000 (OpenWebUI, dev servers, etc.) the login button bounced to that local app. Two compounding causes: (1) `scripts/replace-placeholder.sh` in the calcom container's `command:` referenced `$BUILT_NEXT_PUBLIC_WEBAPP_URL` and `$NEXT_PUBLIC_WEBAPP_URL` with single dollar signs ŌĆö Compose interpolates those at _render_ time against host env / project `.env` (where they are not defined), so the script ran as a no-op against empty strings and 767 bundle references stayed unsubstituted. (2) `BUILT_NEXT_PUBLIC_WEBAPP_URL` was not set in the calcom env block, so even with `$$` escape the script wouldn't have known what FROM string to look for. (3) `ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES=${CALCOM_ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES:-["scheduler.aishacrm.com"]}` had Compose strip the inner double quotes from the `${VAR:-default}` default expression, leaving Cal.com to do `JSON.parse('[scheduler.aishacrm.com]')` (unquoted token ŌåÆ throw ŌåÆ 500 on hostname-validated routes). Patch escapes both vars to `$$` so sh expands at runtime against container env, hardcodes `BUILT_NEXT_PUBLIC_WEBAPP_URL=http://localhost:3000` (matching the calcom/cal.com:latest image's bake-time placeholder), and hardcodes `ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES="scheduler.aishacrm.com"` in YAML single-quote so the inner double-quote chars survive to the container. Live VPS-2 compose + .env edited in place; repo file aligned. Added a 5-test static-analysis regression suite (`calcom-vps2-deploy-config.test.js`) that fails CI if any of the three patterns regresses.

- **AiSHA stack moved into a single `aishacrm.slice` systemd slice for aggregate CPU/memory budgeting (`/etc/systemd/system/aishacrm.slice`, `docker-compose.prod.yml`, `braid-mcp-node-server/docker-compose.prod.yml`)**: Replaced per-container `deploy.resources.limits.cpus` allocations with a single host-level slice that enforces `CPUQuota=500%` (5.0 cores aggregate, 0.5 core headroom under provider's 5.5 sustained cap), `MemoryHigh=8G`/`MemoryMax=12G`. All 8 AiSHA services (`backend`, `frontend`, `litellm`, `redis-memory`, `redis-cache`, `braid-mcp-server`, `braid-mcp-1`, `braid-mcp-2`) now run with `cgroup_parent: aishacrm.slice`. Individual containers free to burst within the envelope; collective sustained usage cannot exceed 5.0 cores. Backend additionally has `mem_limit: 4g`, `mem_reservation: 1g`, and `NODE_OPTIONS=--max-old-space-size=3072` so V8's heap is bounded (prevents GC-pressure CPU spikes from runaway memory). Removed the per-container `deploy.resources.limits` blocks since slice now handles aggregate; eliminates double-throttling and the Compose-v2 `mem_limit` + `deploy.resources.limits.memory` conflict. **Diagnostic outcome**: with all containers slice-confined and using ~0.5 cores actual, host load avg held at ~9.7 ŌĆö confirming the remaining ~9 cores of host load is dockerd/containerd/kernel-migration overhead outside any user slice. The 5.5-core sustained cap is a host-level constraint that no app-side tuning can address; resolution path is migrating to a host with committed CPU. Also fixed: braid-mcp-node-server had a stale invalid `DOPPLER_TOKEN` in its `.env` (using `DOPPLER_TOKEN_PROD` value while backend used the newer rotated one) ŌĆö synced it to the working backend token.

- **scheduler.aishacrm.com flapping fixed by switching cloudflared from QUIC to HTTP/2 (`docker-compose.vps2.yml`)**: Users reported scheduler.aishacrm.com going down and back up periodically. Diagnostic ruled out memory pressure (calcom RestartCount=0, no OOM events, 460MB RAM use within 4GB total host) and ruled out calcom itself (uptime 5h, healthy). Smoking gun in cloudflared logs: all 4 tunnel connections dropped simultaneously with `failed to accept QUIC stream: timeout: no recent network activity`, then reconnected ~8 seconds later. Root cause: cloudflared's default QUIC/UDP transport doesn't survive NAT idle timeouts on budget VPS networks (Zap's upstream NAT recycles idle UDP flows after ~30-60s, killing all connection-keepalive UDP packets). Fix: added `--protocol http2` to the cloudflared command. HTTP/2 over TCP has built-in keepalives that survive NAT timeouts. Verified: all 4 connections re-registered with `protocol=http2`, ingress rule (`scheduler.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ http://calcom:3000`) still applied, no further drop events. Repo `docker-compose.vps2.yml` updated with the flag and a comment explaining the tradeoff.

- **Backend metric/log capture loops throttled (Doppler `aishacrm/prd_prd`: `SYSTEM_METRICS_ENABLED=false`, `PERF_LOG_FLUSH_MS=30000`)**: Searched the backend for periodic loops on the suspicion that high-frequency metric capture was contributing to VPS-1's sustained CPU. Found three: `systemMetrics.collectMetrics()` running every 30s and forking `df -h /` (process-fork is the expensive part on a CPU-constrained host); `perfLogBatcher` flushing every 2s (30 wake-ups/min even with empty queue); frontend `systemLogBatcher` POSTing every 2s. Disabled systemMetrics entirely (the in-memory ring buffer at `/api/monitoring/*` duplicates data already available from Coolify, hosting provider portals, and `docker stats`). Bumped perfLogBatcher flush from 2s ŌåÆ 30s. **Result: backend wake-ups dropped from ~32/min to ~2/min for these loops, but VPS-1 load avg held steady at 8.13.** This rules out polling work as the dominant CPU consumer and pins the cause squarely on kernel migration-thread overhead from container scheduling ŌĆö the next lever is CPU pinning via `cpuset_cpus` (tracked in task #14). Frontend log batcher couldn't be tuned via env ŌĆö `import.meta.env?.VITE_SYSTEM_LOG_BATCH_INTERVAL_MS` is build-time-replaced by Vite, the literal `2000` is baked into the bundle; making it runtime-controllable requires a `getRuntimeEnv()` refactor and image rebuild (queued separately).

- **Ollama brought online on VPS-2, locked down to VPS-1 only (`docker-compose.vps2.yml`, UFW + DOCKER-USER chain)**: `aishacrm-ollama` had been in `Created` (never started) state since deploy, causing every `ollama/*` route in LiteLLM to fail-then-fallback to Groq with extra latency. Removed the orphaned container, brought it up via compose, capped at 1.5 cores. The persistent `ollama_data` volume preserved a `llama3.1:8b` model from a prior session (4.9GB) so no re-download needed. Verified inference end-to-end: cold start 38s for model load, then 14s/token CPU-only generation; warm-state will be substantially faster within the 5-minute keep-alive window. Firewall verified: UFW allows port 11434 only from VPS-1 (147.189.173.237), DOCKER-USER chain has corresponding RETURN for VPS-1 + DROP-all for the destination port. Cross-VPS reachability test from VPS-1 host: TCP succeeded. LiteLLM's `litellm_config.yaml` was already configured to route `ollama/*` and `local/llama3.1:8b` to `http://147.189.168.164:11434` with `groq/*` fallback, so backend code paths using local models now resolve to live Ollama instead of timing out.

- **CampaignWorker poll interval default raised from 5s to 60s (`backend/server.js`, Doppler `aishacrm/prd_prd` `CAMPAIGN_WORKER_INTERVAL_MS=60000`)**: VPS-1 backend logs over a 14.5 min window showed `[CampaignWorker] Tick` 168 times ŌĆö every 5 seconds ŌĆö with `scheduledDue:0, runningActive:0` on every tick. The actual HTTP request volume in the same window was 156 requests (~0.18 req/sec), so request handling wasn't burning CPU; the polling worker was. The hard-coded fallback in `backend/server.js:980` was `5000` even though `.env.example` documented `30000` as the recommended value. Bumped the fallback to 60000 and set the explicit value in Doppler. Verified post-change: ticks dropped from 12/min to 1/min in live logs. Note: load average on the host did not move significantly, confirming the bigger CPU consumer on VPS-1 is kernel migration-thread overhead from the docker container fleet, not request handling ŌĆö followup work (CPU pinning via `cpuset_cpus`, container consolidation) tracked separately.

- **OpenReplay calls eliminated, Microsoft Clarity made the explicit session-replay provider (`frontend-entrypoint.sh`, `docker-compose.prod.yml`, Doppler `aishacrm/prd_prd`)**: After the OpenReplay-to-Clarity migration earlier in 2026, the frontend container kept emitting requests to `https://replay.aishacrm.com/ingest/v1/web/start` because the build-time-baked + container-cached OpenReplay env vars (`VITE_OPENREPLAY_PROJECT_KEY`, `INGEST_POINT`, `DASHBOARD_URL`) were still being injected into `env-config.js` at runtime. Browser console showed CORS errors on every page load. Fix: deleted the six OpenReplay secrets from Doppler, set `VITE_OPENREPLAY_ENABLED=false` (defensive ŌĆö kills the React hook's first check even if a stale bundle has URLs baked in), set `VITE_SESSION_REPLAY_PROVIDER=clarity` (explicit selection), updated `frontend-entrypoint.sh` to fetch + inject the Clarity vars (`VITE_CLARITY_ENABLED`, `VITE_CLARITY_PROJECT_ID`, `VITE_CLARITY_DASHBOARD_URL`) and the new selector/toggle vars into `env-config.js`, removed the OpenReplay normalization block (mapping bare `OPENREPLAY_*` ŌåÆ `VITE_OPENREPLAY_*`), removed the OpenReplay env passthrough from `docker-compose.prod.yml` frontend service. Pushed the new entrypoint to the live VPS-1 container via `docker cp` and restarted; verified `env-config.js` now contains the correct Clarity config and zero `replay.aishacrm.com` references. Note: the React hook code (`useOpenReplay.js`, `OpenReplayControl.jsx`, `@openreplay/tracker` dep) still exists in the bundle ŌĆö full code-level removal is a separate cleanup; the env flag bails the hook before any network call.

- **scheduler.aishacrm.com migrated from cross-VPS public-IP hop to dedicated cloudflared connector on VPS-2 (`docker-compose.vps2.yml`, `cloudflared-config-vps1.yml`, Cloudflare Tunnel `aishacrm-vps2` id `ecff23d3-890e-4bea-b59e-aacbafae4b9c`, Doppler `prd_prd` secrets `TUNNEL_TOKEN_VPS2` + `TUNNEL_ID_VPS2`)**: Previously VPS-1's cloudflared (tunnel `8336e18d-ŌĆ”`) routed `scheduler.aishacrm.com` to `http://147.189.168.164:3002` ŌĆö unencrypted HTTP across the public WAN to VPS-2's exposed calcom port. Created a new tunnel on VPS-2's account, deployed cloudflared as a docker service on the `aishanet` network (capped at 0.3 cores), configured ingress `scheduler.aishacrm.com ŌåÆ http://calcom:3000` (docker-internal). DNS CNAME for `scheduler.aishacrm.com` updated to `ecff23d3-890e-4bea-b59e-aacbafae4b9c.cfargotunnel.com` ŌĆö the `.cfargotunnel.com` suffix matters: without it Cloudflare's edge returns HTTP 530 (origin DNS error 1016). Removed the scheduler ingress rule from VPS-1's `/etc/cloudflared/config.yml`, removed the `3002:3000` host port mapping from calcom on VPS-2, removed the temporary UFW + DOCKER-USER allow for VPS-1ŌåÆVPS-2:3002. Calcom is now reachable only through the tunnel; port 3002 is no longer publicly listening on VPS-2. Verified end-to-end: 200 response with patched bundle (zero `localhost:3000` references), `originService=http://calcom:3000` confirmed in cloudflared logs.

- **VPS-1 sustained CPU usage exceeding provider's 5.5-core cap (`docker-compose.prod.yml`, `braid-mcp-node-server/docker-compose.prod.yml`, `scripts/ufw-vps2.sh`)**: VPS-1 was sitting at ~25% sustained on 32 cores (~8 cores of work) against the provider's 5.5-core sustained cap, triggering throttling alerts. Snapshot showed no single hot container ŌĆö bulk of CPU was kernel migration thread overhead from many unbounded containers competing for the scheduler. Fix: hard-capped every VPS-1 container with `docker update --cpus=N` and persisted the values in their respective compose files. Per-container budget (sums to 4.4 cores, 1.1 core headroom): backend 1.5, frontend 0.5, litellm 0.7, redis-memory 0.3, redis-cache 0.2, braid-mcp-server 0.4, braid-mcp-1 0.2, braid-mcp-2 0.2, coolify-proxy 0.2, coolify-sentinel 0.1, aisha-landing-page 0.1. Coolify-managed containers (coolify-proxy, coolify-sentinel, aisha-landing-page) had their caps applied via runtime `docker update` only ŌĆö those persist across container restart but NOT across Coolify redeploy; for permanence those need to be set in Coolify UI ŌåÆ Server ŌåÆ Resources. The same provider cap concern applies to VPS-2 (currently ~7%, well under), but Phase-2 service migrations (e.g., relocating braid-mcp workers) were de-scoped after discovering the workers share Redis state with the coordinator and aren't trivially "as-is" movable.

- **`/api/tenantintegrations` 500 + `/api/calcom-sync/resolve-link` 404 after VPS split (`docker-compose.vps2.yml`, Doppler `aishacrm/prd_prd` secrets `CALCOM_DB_URL` and `CALCOM_DATABASE_URL`)**: Backend's tenant-integrations and calcom-sync routes call `getCalcomDb()` (backend/lib/calcomDb.js) which opens a `pg.Pool` to `postgresql://calcom:...@calcom-db:5432/calcom`. After moving Cal.com to VPS-2, that hostname only resolved inside VPS-2's docker network and the pool timed out at 5s with `Connection terminated due to connection timeout`. The 404 on `/resolve-link` was a downstream symptom ŌĆö the route gates on a successful DB lookup before falling through to the integration row. Fix: exposed calcom-db on VPS-2 public IP (`ports: 5432:5432`), set `CALCOM_DB_URL` and `CALCOM_DATABASE_URL` in Doppler `prd_prd` to `postgresql://calcom:<pw>@147.189.168.164:5432/calcom`, restarted backend on VPS-1 to pick up the Doppler-injected env. Verified end-to-end: backend connects, queries `current_user=calcom, current_database=calcom`. **Security caveat**: Postgres is now on the public WAN. Mitigations: 43-char random password, SCRAM-SHA-256 (handshake never sends password in the clear). Wire protocol itself is plaintext ŌĆö same exposure profile as the existing cross-VPS HTTP hop for calcom on port 3002. Hardening followups queued: UFW restrict 5432 to VPS-1's IP only; long-term migrate cross-VPS traffic to Tailscale/Wireguard mesh and revert calcom-db to internal-only.

- **Hawser image/port drift between repo and live VPS-2 (`docker-compose.vps2.yml`)**: Repo's compose had `ghcr.io/finsys/hawser:latest` on port 2376; the live VPS-2 install was on `mjohnsongp/hawser:latest` on port 8080. The finsys image fails on Docker 29.x (rejects the newer Engine API version returned by VPS-2's host); the mjohnsongp community fork carries the API-version compat fix. Aligned repo to live so a re-deploy reproduces what's currently working.

### Added

- **Doppler MCP server: added write capability + fixed broken read paths (`doppler-mcp/server.py`, `doppler-mcp/test_set_secrets.py`)**: The custom Python MCP server (`mcpServers.doppler` in `claude_desktop_config.json`) had two bugs: (1) every secret-related read endpoint hit `/v3/secrets*` but Doppler's actual API path is `/v3/configs/config/secrets*`, causing 404 on `list_secrets`, `get_secret`, `get_secrets`, and `download_secrets`; project/config reads worked because those paths were correct. (2) The MCP exposed only read tools ŌĆö no way to update secrets from a session. Patched all four secret-related GET paths and added a new `doppler_set_secrets` tool (POST `/v3/configs/config/secrets`) that supports both writing values and deleting (`null` value). Added `_api_post` helper and `SetSecretsInput` Pydantic model. New `test_set_secrets.py` covers the corrected paths and the new tool with mock-based unit tests (9 tests passing) ŌĆö confirms `set_secrets` posts to the right endpoint, distinguishes write-vs-delete via null values, short-circuits on empty payload, and that `list_secrets`/`get_secret` now hit the corrected paths. Required for any future session that needs to manage secrets across `dev_personal`, `stg_stg`, `prd_prd` configs without falling back to the Doppler CLI.
- **Doppler MCP token sync helper (`scripts/sync-doppler-mcp-token.ps1`)**: Idempotent PowerShell script that reads `DOPPLER_ACCESS_TOKEN` from the repo's `.env` and writes it into `claude_desktop_config.json`'s `mcpServers.doppler.env.DOPPLER_TOKEN`. Backs up the config first (`*.bak-<timestamp>`), preserves UTF-8-without-BOM, validates the token format (`dp.pt.*`), and prints next steps (kill stale Python processes, full Claude Desktop restart). Solves the "I rotated my token but the MCP still 401s" gap where the Doppler dashboard rotation doesn't propagate to the MCP server's env config.
- **Microsoft Clarity session replay support + provider-agnostic abstraction (`src/hooks/useClarity.js`, `src/hooks/useSessionReplay.js`, `src/hooks/useSessionReplayTracking.js`)**: Added Clarity as a lightweight, SaaS-only alternative to OpenReplay after the latter's container stack was identified as the trigger for the 5-hour VPS crash cycle on the production VPS (32-core box capped at 550% CPU by the hosting provider). New `useClarity` hook matches `useOpenReplay`'s public interface (`isInitialized`, `setUserInfo`, `enableAssist`, `trackEvent`, `getSessionUrl`) so it's a drop-in via a new `useSessionReplay` selector that switches on `VITE_SESSION_REPLAY_PROVIDER` (`clarity` | `openreplay` | `none`). `App.jsx` now mounts `useSessionReplayTracking` instead of `useOpenReplayTracking`; the old hook remains in place for back-compat. Existing `VITE_OPENREPLAY_ENABLED=true` deployments continue working without code changes via fallback resolution.
- **Live take-over button via Jitsi/Whereby/Meet (`src/components/support/RequestHelp.jsx`)**: Companion to Clarity (which lacks remote take-over). Generates a unique meeting URL on click (default: public Jitsi room, no signup), opens it for the user, optionally POSTs to a notify webhook (`VITE_HELP_NOTIFY_URL`) so the support operator can join. Provider switchable via `VITE_HELP_MEETING_PROVIDER` (`jitsi` | `whereby` | `meet`); host overridable via `VITE_HELP_MEETING_BASE_URL` for self-hosted Jitsi.
- **Lockup diagnostic script + tests (`scripts/lockup-diagnostic.sh`, `scripts/lockup-diagnostic.test.sh`)**: Read-only diagnostic for VPS lockup investigation. Pulls VPS-side evidence (kernel, journalctl, sar, docker, cron, auth, disk, redis SLOWLOG) and Cloudflare-side evidence (HTTP analytics + 5xx breakdown via GraphQL Analytics API, `cloudflared` tunnel journal) for a configurable time window, bundles into a tarball. Auto-loads `CLOUDFLARE_ACCESS_TOKEN` from `.env` if present. Companion test suite (7 tests) caught a real GNU-date arithmetic bug ŌĆö string-form `"$TS - 15 minutes"` is mis-parsed as a TZ offset (returns 17:01 instead of 01:45); script now uses epoch math.

### Changed

- **`.env.example` Session Replay block restructured**: collapsed legacy OpenReplay-only block into a provider-agnostic structure with `VITE_SESSION_REPLAY_PROVIDER`, separate Clarity sub-block (`VITE_CLARITY_ENABLED`, `VITE_CLARITY_PROJECT_ID`, `VITE_CLARITY_DASHBOARD_URL`), preserved OpenReplay sub-block, plus new Live Take-Over section (`VITE_HELP_MEETING_PROVIDER`, `VITE_HELP_MEETING_BASE_URL`, `VITE_HELP_NOTIFY_URL`).
- **`src/App.jsx` swapped `useOpenReplayTracking` ŌåÆ `useSessionReplayTracking`**: provider-agnostic mount; back-compat preserved via env fallback in `useSessionReplay`.

- **Coolify staging deployment skeleton (`staging/`)**: 5 Docker Compose resources mapping to the user's deployment groups (1: backend-heavy, 2: app-fast, 3: ai-infra, 4: braid, 5: scheduling-rare). Containers are prefixed `staging-`, share an external `staging-aishanet` network, and consume Doppler `stg_stg` secrets at runtime. Phase 1 (Redis-only) is gated by `COMPOSE_PROFILES`, so the same `staging/01-backend-heavy/docker-compose.yml` covers both the validation deploy and the full backend deploy without churn. No host ports collide with production (4000/4001/6379/6380/8000/3002/4002/11436); only `127.0.0.1:6479` and `127.0.0.1:6480` are exposed for SSH-tunnel Redis debugging. Public ingress goes through Coolify Traefik (`staging-app|api|scheduler.aishacrm.com`); no Caddy/Hawser changes. Existing GHCR build pipeline (`.github/workflows/docker-release.yml`) and `/opt/aishacrm` production deploy remain untouched.
- **Staging validation scripts (`staging/scripts/`)**: `validate-compose.sh` lints all 5 compose files locally (syntax, container-name uniqueness, host-port uniqueness, prod-port collision check, network membership). `post-deploy-check.sh` runs phase-aware smoke tests on the App VPS ŌĆö verifies expected containers are healthy, hits HTTP health endpoints over `staging-aishanet`, and confirms both Redis instances answer `PING`.
- **Staging operations guide (`staging/README.md`)**: container/port map, Doppler `stg_stg` bootstrap instructions, DNS records, Coolify resource setup, 6-phase rollout sequence, branch strategy options, coexistence model with current GHCR-based prod deploy.
- **Litellm + cal.com bind-mount fix for Coolify v4 (`staging/03-ai-infra/litellm_config.yaml`, `staging/05-scheduling-rare/calcom-db-init.sql`)**: Coolify v4 mishandles `..` segments in compose volume sources; when the source can't be resolved, Docker bind-creates an empty directory at the source path and the container then sees a directory at the mount target. Symptom on first deploy: `IsADirectoryError: [Errno 21] Is a directory: '/app/config.yaml'` on litellm; same defect would have hit calcom-db on its init script. Fix: keep a local copy of the source-of-truth file inside each group folder so the bind path is `./<file>`, no `..`. `validate-compose.sh` extended with a drift check (`cmp -s` against the repo-root original) so the staging copies cannot silently diverge from `litellm_config.yaml` and `scripts/calcom-db-init.sql`.
- **Doppler stg_stg bootstrap script (`staging/scripts/bootstrap-stg_stg.sh`)**: idempotent local script that creates the `stg_stg` config in the `aishacrm` Doppler project (which currently does not exist ŌĆö only the `stg` root environment is present), bulk-clones every `prd_prd` secret, applies staging URL/origin overrides, optionally rotates Cal.com cryptographic secrets (`--rotate-calcom`), and mints a `stg_stg`-scoped service token for Coolify. Required because the `DOPPLER_TOKEN` in the repo's `.env` is a service token (`dp.st.*`) scoped read-only to `prd_prd` and cannot create configs or write to other configs ŌĆö workplace writes need a personal token via `doppler login`.
- **Doppler bootstrap (Python, REST-only) (`staging/scripts/bootstrap-stg_stg.py` + `test_bootstrap_stg_stg.py`)**: pure-`urllib` equivalent of the bash bootstrap, suitable for sandboxed/CI environments where the Doppler CLI cannot be installed and the `doppler login` browser flow is unavailable. Same six steps (auth verify ŌåÆ create stg_stg ŌåÆ clone 149 secrets from prd_prd ŌåÆ apply 8 URL overrides ŌåÆ rotate Cal.com ŌåÆ mint Coolify service token), driven by a `dp.pt.*` personal access token in `DOPPLER_PERSONAL_TOKEN` env var. 11 unit tests cover request shaping, meta-key exclusion, override coverage, CSPRNG rotation, and PAT-vs-service-token gating.
- **Coolify staging provisioner (Python, REST API) (`staging/scripts/provision-coolify.py`)**: idempotent, dry-run-capable script that creates the Coolify project `aishacrm-staging` and 5 docker-compose applications on the App VPS (server `beige-koala`/`f7uzrwlbqjtx6qamppma5xsz`/`147.189.173.237`), populates 61 env vars across the 5 apps (DOPPLER_TOKEN/PROJECT/CONFIG plus per-group overrides drawn from `staging/.env.example`), and attaches FQDNs only to groups 1/2/5 via Coolify's `docker_compose_domains` mapping. Manifest of created UUIDs persists to `staging/.coolify-manifest.json` so re-runs reuse rather than duplicate. 9 unit tests cover group definitions, FQDN-only-on-public-groups, Doppler token propagation, Phase 1 `COMPOSE_PROFILES=""` gate, Cal.com secret-spread (only groups 1 and 5), and the dockercompose REST contract (`POST /api/v1/applications/public` with `build_pack=dockercompose` and `docker_compose_domains: [{name, domain}]`).

### Fixed

- **Coolify migration goals/achievements/next-steps doc (`docs/deployment/COOLIFY_MIGRATION.md`)**: Captured the full strategic context for the GHCR-replacement workstream ŌĆö original brief (cut GHA + GHCR costs, Coolify-native builds), constraints from the 2026-04-26 brief, complete Phase 1 (staging POC) results including all Coolify v4 quirks discovered (container_name ignored, `..` segments stripped, dotenv quote stripping, manifest schema v1 unsupported, dockerignore pattern interactions, force=true ŌēĀ pull always), operational learnings (OOM incident, on-demand wind-down, security cleanup), and the Phase 2 (production migration) roadmap with per-service order, recipe, and pre-migration hardening checklist. Cross-linked from `staging/README.md` and `orchestra/PLAN.md` so future sessions following the orchestra control layer per `CLAUDE.md` will find the active workstream.

- **All staging Coolify resources stopped, environment moved to on-demand (`staging/README.md`)**: Stopped staging-backend-heavy, staging-app-fast, staging-ai-infra, staging-braid, and staging-tunnel via Coolify API after evaluating that the maintenance/resource cost of an always-on staging duplicate of every prod service didn't pay for itself in this project's solo-team / CI-tested context. The OOM-class incident that took down both prod and staging containers on the App VPS in late April 2026 was the proximate cause. Coolify resources, compose files, custom GHCR images (`aishacrm-2-litellm`, `aishacrm-2-calcom-db`), and the `staging-aishanet` external network all remain in place so staging can be brought back up on demand for specific exercises (deploy-pipeline migration, multi-service integration tests). README rewritten with wind-down rationale and on-demand quick-start. Validated freed VPS resource: ~1 GB RAM and several CPU% returned to prod.

- **Group 5 (`staging-scheduling-rare`) marked opt-in (`staging/README.md`)**: Paused the Coolify resource for staging-scheduling-rare via API (POST `/api/v1/applications/{uuid}/stop`). Reasoning: Cal.com is third-party infrastructure (release cadence, manifest schema, ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES env parsing, postgres init-script bind mounts all owned upstream) and adds no validation value to the AiSHA deploy pipeline ŌĆö the backend talks to it via HTTP and a missing scheduler is a valid staging state. Production uses the same `profiles: [scheduling]` opt-in pattern in `docker-compose.prod.yml`. The compose file, custom `aishacrm-2-calcom-db` GHCR image, env wiring, and ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES quote-preservation fix remain in the repo so the resource can be resumed any time via Coolify UI ŌåÆ Start.

- **Cal.com `ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES` quote-stripping under Coolify (`staging/05-scheduling-rare/docker-compose.yml`)**: After repinning to Cal.com v6.2.0, the calcom container crash-looped with `SyntaxError: Unexpected token 's', "[staging-sc"... is not valid JSON`. Cal.com middleware does `JSON.parse('[' + process.env.ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES + ']')`, so the value must be a JSON-string literal (i.e. include the double-quote characters). The previous default `${CALCOM_ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES:-"staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com"}` carried the inner quotes through Docker Compose interpolation in standalone deploys, but Coolify's render ŌåÆ .env file ŌåÆ dotenv-parse ŌåÆ container-env pipeline strips outer quotes per dotenv spec. YAML-quoted the entire env entry (`'ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES=${CALCOM_ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES:-"staging-scheduler.aishacrm.com"}'`) so the inner double-quotes survive verbatim through every layer.

- **Staging Cal.com image pin updated for Docker 28.2.2 manifest support (`staging/05-scheduling-rare/docker-compose.yml`)**: The production-pinned digest `calcom/cal.com@sha256:0aca8203...` (v5.x-era image, validated 2026-04-07 in prod) failed to pull on the App VPS with `Error response from daemon: unknown: manifest schema unsupported`. Modern Docker (28.2.2 on `beige-koala`) has dropped support for the legacy Docker Registry V1-style manifest schema that image was pushed with. Repinned staging to `calcom/cal.com@sha256:ace3bb1219fb7306585ab9f4d94d41af7ee064c343db0498173436bbe857bd49` ŌĆö Cal.com v6.2.0, released 2026-03-02, current `:latest`, OCI v2 manifest. Production compose unchanged (production may still have the v5 image cached locally; bumping prod to this same v6.2.0 digest is recommended after revalidating Host table, `_user_eventtype`, and `ALLOWED_HOSTNAMES`).

- **`.dockerignore` was excluding `scripts/calcom-db-init.sql` from the calcom-db build context** (`.dockerignore`): The new `aishacrm-2-calcom-db` GHCR build (v7.1.20 tag) failed at the `COPY scripts/calcom-db-init.sql /docker-entrypoint-initdb.d/` step because two `.dockerignore` patterns filtered the file out of the build context ŌĆö `scripts/` (line 50) and `*.sql` (line 59). When the calcom-db job failed, the matrix cancelled the other 4 in-flight image builds. Fix: appended `!scripts/calcom-db-init.sql` re-include after the broad excludes so Docker's ignore matcher applies the negation last; this is BuildKit-supported behavior (the workflow uses `docker/build-push-action@v5`). Required pushing v7.1.21 to retrigger the matrix.

- **Cal.com postgres container crash on Coolify staging deploy (`calcom-db/Dockerfile`, `staging/05-scheduling-rare/docker-compose.yml`)**: Same Coolify-v4 compose-rendering quirk that broke litellm ŌĆö the bind mount for `scripts/calcom-db-init.sql` resolved to a non-existent path, Docker auto-created an empty directory at the source, and postgres-entrypoint failed to source the file. Fix: new `aishacrm-2-calcom-db` GHCR image (`FROM postgres:15-alpine` + `COPY scripts/calcom-db-init.sql /docker-entrypoint-initdb.d/`), built by `docker-release.yml` matrix. Staging compose swapped from stock `postgres:15-alpine` (with bind mount) to `ghcr.io/andreibyf/aishacrm-2-calcom-db:${CALCOM_DB_IMAGE_TAG:-latest}` (no bind mount). The init script runs once on first cluster init per postgres-entrypoint convention; the existing `staging_calcom_db_data` named volume continues to persist data across image upgrades. Production `docker-compose.prod.yml` keeps its bind mount (works there because GHA SCPs the script to `/opt/aishacrm/scripts/`); the baked-in copy matches by SHA. Drift check for `calcom-db-init.sql` removed from `validate-compose.sh` ŌĆö `MIRRORS` array is now empty, no staging file dependencies remain on the bind-mount path.

- **Litellm container crash-loop on Coolify staging deploy (`litellm/Dockerfile`, `staging/03-ai-infra/docker-compose.yml`)**: Coolify v4 in compose deployment mode renders only the compose file into the application's working directory ŌĆö it does NOT clone the repo working tree.
